# Executive Summary

Novaworks – CVC/Strategic Investment Executive Summary

## Overview

Novaworks is building an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform on ServiceNow to solve the inefficiency of legacy systems for the deskless workforce. This memo informs a decision to make a $1M strategic seed investment, and we recommend proceeding due to the venture's exceptional alignment with ServiceNow's strategy to extend the Now Platform into a core system of record and directly challenge incumbents like Workday.

## Strategic Opportunity Fit

Strategic Opportunity Fit – Strong fit. This venture directly supports ServiceNow's corporate strategy by creating a native, AI-driven HCM system of record on the Now Platform, leveraging our brand, go-to-market channels, and data fabric to displace competitors from within our own customer base.

## Execution Roadmap

The investment thesis requires Novaworks to successfully build its MVP on an aggressive timeline and convert its "customer zero" partners, including ServiceNow, into paid pilots that validate both the technology and the premium pricing model. The primary execution risks are the significant challenge of building a complex enterprise product from a standstill and the critical dependency on formalizing the co-sell and IP licensing partnership with ServiceNow, which is currently based on verbal agreements.

## Venture Opportunity Snapshot

The large Human Capital Management market is primed for AI-led disruption, especially for the historically underserved deskless workforce segment. Novaworks' approach of building an AI-native solution directly on the Now Platform creates a unique opportunity to displace competitors like Workday by offering a more integrated, modern, and cost-effective alternative to our shared enterprise customers.

---

## Analysis

**Team & Execution:** **Exceptional founder-market fit, but key-person risk is high.** The founding team combines prior entrepreneurial exits with deep ServiceNow experience, providing unique credibility and an ability to navigate our ecosystem. However, execution capability is dangerously concentrated in the three founders, and the critical Chief Data & AI Officer role remains unfilled, posing a risk to its "AI-native" promise.

**Market (TAM) & Trends:** **Large, validated market with strong AI tailwinds.** The $34.1B HCM market is rapidly adopting AI, creating a clear window of opportunity for a challenger. The venture's focus on the underserved deskless workforce provides a strategic entry point, though its claimed $12B serviceable market is an unverified company estimate that requires further validation.

**Technology & Solution:** **Strong vision, but pre-product with IP risks.** The AI-native, agentic architecture built on ServiceNow is a compelling technical differentiator that aligns perfectly with our platform strategy. However, the company is pre-product with no existing IP, and its reliance on a verbal agreement for ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" IP—which includes a grant-back clause—is a significant legal risk that we must help formalize and de-risk.

**Traction & Validation:** **Zero traction; validation depends entirely on unverified partner commitments.** As a pre-product company, there is no revenue or customer validation. The entire investment thesis rests on converting claimed "customer zero" commitments from ServiceNow and Bell Canada into paid pilots, which is the most critical near-term milestone to de-risk the opportunity.

**Terms, Finance & Operations:** **Unrealistic financial model and a tight runway.** The financial projections, particularly the 105.7x LTV/CAC ratio and a 2.3-month payback period, are not credible and rely on unproven channel efficiencies. The requested $7M seed round provides a tight 15-month runway with little buffer for delays, and the model contains internal inconsistencies regarding headcount and gross margins that must be reconciled.

## Critical Open Questions

- How formal are the "customer zero" commitments from ServiceNow's internal business units and Bell Canada, and what is their true willingness to pay for a pilot at a material price point?
- Can the verbal agreement for ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" IP be formalized into a written license with terms that provide Novaworks with sufficient freedom to operate and build value without encumbering its future IP?
- Is the proposed $7M seed round sufficient to reach meaningful validation milestones (i.e., multiple paid pilots) given the 6-9 month enterprise sales cycle and significant product development required from a standing start?
- What is a realistic, bottoms-up financial model for customer acquisition cost and gross margin, and does the business remain viable under more conservative, industry-benchmarked assumptions?
- Who is in the pipeline for the critical Chief Data & AI Officer role, and can this position be filled quickly to guide the core product build and validate the "AI-native" thesis?



# Executive Summary - 10 Pager

## Overview

Novaworks presents a high-risk, high-reward strategic investment opportunity for ServiceNow. The venture aims to build an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform directly on the Now Platform, targeting the large, underserved deskless workforce to compete with incumbents like Workday. The founding team, which includes former ServiceNow executives, provides exceptional strategic alignment and insider knowledge. However, the company is pre-product and pre-revenue, facing significant execution, financial, and legal risks. The core investment thesis is contingent on validating unverified customer commitments and formalizing a critical but currently verbal partnership with ServiceNow. The recommendation is to proceed with focused diligence to address these fundamental uncertainties before committing capital.

## Key Takeaways

*   **Exceptional Strategic Fit**: Novaworks' mission to build a native HCM on the Now Platform directly supports ServiceNow's strategy to become a system of record and displace competitors like Workday from within its own customer base.
*   **Experienced Founding Team**: The team, led by a former ServiceNow executive, possesses deep domain expertise, prior entrepreneurial success, and invaluable insider knowledge of the ServiceNow ecosystem.
*   **Large Market Opportunity**: The venture targets the large and growing $34.1B HCM market, with a strategic focus on the underserved deskless workforce and the market-wide shift to AI-driven solutions.
*   **Unproven Execution Plan**: The company is pre-product and pre-revenue, with an aggressive development timeline, an unreliable financial model containing internal inconsistencies, and a critical leadership gap for the Chief Data & AI Officer role.
*   **Critical External Dependencies**: Success is entirely contingent on formalizing a verbal IP and co-sell agreement with ServiceNow and validating unconfirmed "customer zero" commitments, which currently lack evidence of a true willingness to pay.

## Risks

*   **Execution Risk**: The venture is pre-product and must build a complex enterprise solution from a standstill on an aggressive 15-month timeline with a tight budget and a key leadership gap in the Chief Data & AI Officer role.
*   **Financial Viability Risk**: The financial model is not credible, with unrealistic unit economics (105.7x LTV/CAC), internal inconsistencies on headcount, and an insufficient 15-month runway that leaves no margin for common enterprise sales cycle or product development delays.
*   **Partnership & IP Risk**: The entire business model depends on a verbal agreement with ServiceNow for IP licensing and go-to-market support. The IP agreement includes a grant-back clause that could encumber Novaworks' future value and must be formalized.
*   **Market Validation Risk**: There is no revenue or product validation. The investment thesis rests on unverified "customer zero" commitments from ServiceNow and Bell Canada, with no evidence of their willingness to pay a premium price for a pilot.

## Next Steps

*   **Validate Customer Commitments**: Secure formal, written, paid pilot agreements from at least two of the three "customer zero" partners to confirm market demand and willingness-to-pay at a material price point.
*   **Formalize ServiceNow Partnership**: Execute a definitive written agreement for the IP license (clarifying the grant-back clause) and the co-sell partnership within 90 days of investment.
*   **Rebuild Financial Model**: Develop a credible, bottoms-up 24-month operating budget and financial model that reconciles the hiring plan with expenses and demonstrates sufficient runway.
*   **Secure AI Leadership**: Fill the vacant Chief Data & AI Officer role to provide the necessary technical leadership to guide the product build and de-risk the "AI-native" thesis.

| $34.1B TAM and $12B SAM | [DOC: Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx, p. 1] | The $34.1B TAM is validated by third-party reports. The $12B SAM is a company estimate with no provided methodology and is considered unverified, as noted in the *Analysis* table. | High (TAM), Low (SAM) |
| "Customer Zero" Commitments | [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown] | Commitments from ServiceNow and Bell Canada are claimed but are currently verbal and unverified. This is a primary diligence risk highlighted throughout the analysis. | Very Low |
| 105.7x LTV/CAC Ratio | [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 11] | This projection is not credible for a pre-revenue company and is based on unproven assumptions about a low CAC via the ServiceNow channel and high premium pricing. | Very Low |
| AI-Native Differentiation | [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown] | The architectural concept is a strong differentiator, but the company is pre-product with no IP and a vacant Chief Data & AI Officer role. The claim is currently a vision, not a reality. | Low |

## Overview
Novaworks is building an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform on ServiceNow to solve the inefficiency of legacy systems for the deskless workforce. This memo informs a decision on a $1M strategic seed investment, and we recommend proceeding due to the venture's exceptional alignment with ServiceNow's strategy to extend the Now Platform into a core system of record and directly challenge incumbents like Workday.

## Strategic Opportunity Fit

## Tell it to me straight
> Let's be clear. This isn't an investment in a company; it's a $1M call option on owning the native HCM for our platform. The real asset here is Kelley Steven-Waiss. She's one of us—a former ServiceNow exec and a CHRO who knows the platform, the buyers, and the problem inside and out. She's assembled a team with prior exits to build an HCM on our turf specifically to go after Workday's customers within our own accounts. Strategically, it's a perfect fit.
>
> But right now, it's all just a story. They're pre-product, pre-revenue, and have zero IP. The financial model is a joke—100x LTV/CAC is fantasy. The whole thing hinges on two questions: can they actually build this complex product on a shoestring budget, and can they turn their verbal handshakes with us and Bell Canada into real, paying contracts?
>
> The biggest landmine is the legal mess with our own IP. They have a "verbal agreement" with a grant-back clause that could give us a headache later. We need to get that in writing and de-fanged before we wire a dime. This is an outsourced R&D project with a world-class team that could become a massive strategic asset or a quick acqui-hire. Our job is to lock down the IP terms and force them to prove someone will actually pay for this thing.

### Should We Do It? (Strategic Attractiveness & Fit)

**Strategic Attractiveness of the Prize:** The opportunity is large, durable, and strategically vital. Novaworks targets the $34.1 billion Human Capital Management (HCM) market, which is projected to grow at a 9.6% compound annual growth rate [DOC: Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx, p. 1], [Fortune Business Insights](https://www.fortunebusinessinsights.com/industry-reports/human-capital-management-hcm-market-100240). The venture focuses on two high-priority segments: the historically underserved deskless workforce, which comprises 80% of global employees, and the market-wide shift toward AI-native solutions [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. With AI in HR being the top emerging technology priority for HR leaders, the timing is opportune to capture a share of a market undergoing significant modernization [DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 9].

**Strategic Fit with the Organization:** The venture's alignment with ServiceNow's corporate strategy is exceptionally strong. Novaworks is building its solution *on* the ServiceNow platform, directly supporting the strategic goal of extending the Now Platform into a core system of record for every major enterprise workflow [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. This creates a native, AI-driven HCM system that enables ServiceNow to directly challenge incumbents like Workday within its own customer base, a scenario explicitly described as a "Workday take out" [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. This makes the venture a core strategic play, not an adjacent or exploratory bet.

**Strategic Edge / Unfair Advantage:** ServiceNow provides a powerful and unique advantage as the venture's primary partner. Novaworks can leverage ServiceNow's enterprise-grade platform, which mitigates customer concerns about security and scalability that typically hinder startups [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. Furthermore, ServiceNow's established go-to-market channels, brand credibility, and existing customer relationships provide a distribution advantage that would otherwise take years and significant capital to build. The planned use of ServiceNow's Workflow Data Fabric and AI infrastructure further deepens this symbiotic relationship, creating a technical and commercial edge that standalone competitors cannot replicate [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown].

Should we do it? – Yes (High confidence).
Summary rationale: The venture targets a large, strategically vital market and aligns perfectly with ServiceNow's platform strategy, providing a unique corporate advantage to win.

### Can We Do It? (Execution Capacity & Control)

**Hard Assets (Physical/Financial Capacity):** ServiceNow possesses the two critical hard assets required for this venture to succeed: the financial capital to participate in the $7M seed round and, most importantly, the Now Platform itself [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. The platform serves as the foundational technical infrastructure, providing Novaworks with a secure, scalable, and enterprise-ready environment from day one. This eliminates the need for the venture to build its own core infrastructure, dramatically reducing capital requirements and accelerating time-to-market.

**Market Relationship (Market Access):** ServiceNow's ability to provide market access is a core strength of this opportunity. The venture's go-to-market strategy is designed to target ServiceNow's existing enterprise customers, particularly those in the underpenetrated commercial HRSD segment [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown]. ServiceNow's global sales force has established relationships with the target buyers—CIOs and CHROs—which Novaworks can leverage through the proposed co-sell partnership [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. This direct channel to a qualified customer base significantly de-risks the initial customer acquisition phase.

**Soft Assets (People & Skills):** The venture is led by a team with exceptional "corporate fluency" within the ServiceNow ecosystem. The CEO is a former Chief Innovation Officer at ServiceNow, providing invaluable insider knowledge for navigating the technical and political landscape of the partnership [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. However, a critical execution risk exists within the venture team itself. As an "AI-native" company, the unfilled Chief Data & AI Officer role represents a significant capability gap that threatens its core technical promise and product roadmap, a risk also noted in the *Analysis* table [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown].

Can we do it? – Yes (Medium confidence).
Summary rationale: ServiceNow provides the critical platform and market access, and the team has the right insider experience, but execution risk is elevated by the venture's pre-product status and a key leadership gap.

### Synthesis & Recommendation

The strategic rationale for this investment is compelling. The venture represents a capital-efficient opportunity for ServiceNow to accelerate its platform strategy, enter the core HCM market, and create a formidable competitor to Workday. The "Should we do it?" analysis is a clear "Yes," as the market is attractive and the strategic fit is nearly perfect. The "Can we do it?" analysis is also positive, as ServiceNow provides the essential platform, capital, and market access needed for success.

However, the execution capacity resides almost entirely within the pre-product, pre-revenue Novaworks team. While the founders are highly credible, their success depends on flawlessly executing an aggressive roadmap and formalizing a complex partnership that currently rests on verbal agreements. The investment allows ServiceNow to catalyze a strategically critical solution while containing risk within a partner-led model. The primary task of due diligence is to gain confidence that the venture's operational plan is as sound as its strategic vision.

**Continue Due Diligence**

The next phase of work must focus on de-risking the execution plan by addressing three critical uncertainties:
1.  **Partnership Formalization:** Can the verbal agreements for ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" IP license and the co-sell partnership be formalized into a definitive, written contract that protects both parties' interests?
2.  **Customer Validation:** How firm are the "customer zero" commitments from ServiceNow and Bell Canada, and what is their true willingness to pay a material price for an initial pilot?
3.  **AI Leadership:** What is the plan and candidate pipeline for filling the critical Chief Data & AI Officer role to ensure the "AI-native" thesis can be executed?

### Opportunity Validation

The opportunity is rooted in solving the significant operational and financial burdens of legacy Human Capital Management (HCM) systems, which are ill-equipped for modern workforce demands [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. HR teams spend up to 57% of their time on administrative work, with each manual data entry costing an average of $4.86 [Eddy](https://eddy.com/blog/the-hidden-costs-of-manual-hr/). This problem is most acute for the "deskless" workforce, a segment comprising 80% of global employees that has been historically underserved by traditional HCM technology [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown]. Novaworks proposes an AI-native HCM platform built on ServiceNow to automate these workflows and provide a unified, conversational experience.

Demand for such a solution is supported by strong market signals. A 2023 Gartner survey identified AI in HR technology as the top emerging priority for HR leaders, indicating a clear market pull for modernization [DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 9]. The most direct evidence for Novaworks' specific solution is its claim that ServiceNow and Bell Canada—both current Workday customers—have agreed to serve as "customer zero" design partners [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. However, as noted in the *Analysis* table, these commitments are currently unverified and represent the most critical assumption requiring validation.

### Market Summary

The venture targets the global HCM market, which is large and expanding. The Total Addressable Market (TAM) is estimated at $34.1 billion for 2025, with a projected compound annual growth rate (CAGR) of 9.6% through 2032 [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 6], [Fortune Business Insights](https://www.fortunebusinessinsights.com/industry-reports/human-capital-management-hcm-market-100240). While the company claims a Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) of $12 billion by focusing on the deskless workforce, this is a company-provided estimate that lacks a transparent methodology and is considered low-confidence, as highlighted in the *Claims* table above [DOC: Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx, p. 1].

The most significant market trend is the enterprise-wide push to adopt AI, which is creating a clear window of opportunity for a challenger with an AI-first architecture. Novaworks' strategy is to establish a beachhead by targeting a specific niche: mid-sized enterprises (2,000-7,500 employees) that are already invested in the ServiceNow platform [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 11, 14]. This approach leverages the convergence of two powerful market forces: the urgent demand for AI-driven HR modernization and the strategic focus on the large, underserved deskless worker segment.

### Competitive Landscape

| Competitor / Category | Core Strength | Key Weakness / Gap |
| :--- | :--- | :--- |
| **Incumbents (Workday, Oracle)** | Comprehensive feature suites, large enterprise customer base, and strong brand recognition. | Legacy architecture that is not AI-native, expensive, and slow to implement; not optimized for deskless workers [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. |
| **Modern Challengers (Rippling, UKG)** | Strong user experience and modern cloud-native platforms. UKG has a strong focus on workforce management for deskless employees. | Lack deep, native integration with a major enterprise workflow platform like ServiceNow. |
| **ServiceNow (as Partner/Competitor)** | Owns the underlying platform, providing distribution, security, and data fabric advantages. | Has a strong HR Service Delivery (HRSD) offering but lacks a native, full-suite Core HR system of record, creating the gap Novaworks aims to fill [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown]. |

The competitive dynamic is primarily ecosystem-based. Novaworks is not competing on feature parity alone but on its unique position as a native application within the ServiceNow ecosystem. The "White Space" for the venture is the specific intersection of three attributes: an AI-native architecture, a dedicated focus on the deskless workforce, and native integration with the Now Platform. No single competitor currently occupies this niche, creating a distinct market opening. However, this advantage is fragile, as ServiceNow's own strategic moves, such as its recent collaboration with UKG, could narrow this opening [ServiceNow](https://newsroom.servicenow.com/press-releases/details/2025/ServiceNow-and-UKG-Collaborate-to-Supercharge-Employee-Productivity-and-Efficiency-With-Agentic-AI/default.aspx).

### Regulatory & Legal Landscape Summary

Regulation and intellectual property (IP) represent significant hurdles for Novaworks, not defensible moats. The venture's core function—using AI for employment and workforce management—places its product in a "high-risk" category under emerging global regulations like the European Union's AI Act [Cimplifi](https://www.cimplifi.com/resources/the-updated-state-of-ai-regulations-for-2025/?utm_source=openai). This classification will impose stringent and costly compliance obligations related to data governance, transparency, and human oversight before the product can be sold in key international markets.

From an IP perspective, the company is starting with no proprietary assets, having intentionally avoided development to prevent IP contamination from the founders' prior employment [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. More critically, its plan relies on a "verbal agreement" to license core "Skills Intelligence" IP from ServiceNow. This informal arrangement includes a grant-back clause that requires Novaworks to share back any modifications, creating a material risk that could encumber the value and exclusivity of its own future IP [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. Without formalizing this license and developing a clear compliance roadmap, the legal and regulatory landscape presents a substantial barrier to entry.

### Meta-Analysis: Is This a Valid Opportunity?

The external opportunity is fundamentally valid but highly conditional and carries significant exogenous risks. The validity is rooted in a well-defined problem: legacy HCM systems are inefficient and fail to serve the 80% of the global workforce that is deskless [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown]. This is coupled with a powerful market catalyst, as AI adoption has become the top emerging technology priority for HR leaders, creating a clear demand for modernization [DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 9]. Novaworks targets a defensible white space at the intersection of AI-native architecture, a deskless-worker focus, and native ServiceNow integration that no single incumbent or modern challenger currently occupies.

However, the opportunity's attractiveness is conditional on validating several critical external assumptions. The most direct evidence of demand—commitments from "customer zero" partners like ServiceNow and Bell Canada—remains unverified [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. The venture's entire strategic position is predicated on a partnership with ServiceNow that is not yet formalized, and its IP position is encumbered by a verbal agreement with a grant-back clause [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. Therefore, while the market problem, timing, and competitive positioning create an attractive theoretical opportunity, its real-world viability is contingent on securing tangible customer commitments and formalizing the critical partnership and IP agreements that underpin the entire strategy.

## Product & Technology Path

Novaworks' product path is to build an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform from a complete standstill, as no code has been written to date to avoid intellectual property conflicts [CHAPTER: product-and-technology]. The solution is architected for deep integration with the ServiceNow platform, leveraging its core infrastructure, AI components, and a verbal agreement for its Skills Intelligence IP. The core innovation is a conversational "super agent" designed to automate HR workflows for the deskless workforce through an agentic architecture. The roadmap is highly accelerated, aiming to deliver a functional Minimum Viable Product (MVP) within 15 months to align with key industry events [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. This path carries significant execution risk, centered on the team's ability to orchestrate a complex multi-cloud architecture involving ServiceNow, public clouds, and third-party LLMs on an aggressive timeline [CHAPTER: product-and-technology].

## Go-to-Market Path

The go-to-market path is a phased strategy that is entirely dependent on a cornerstone partnership with ServiceNow. The initial entry point targets mid-market organizations with large deskless workforces that are already within the ServiceNow ecosystem, aiming to reduce adoption friction [CHAPTER: gtm-and-partners]. The commercialization plan begins with founder-led sales to secure "Customer Zero" partners like ServiceNow and Bell Canada, with the primary goal of converting them into 3-5 paid pilots within the 15-month seed runway. Success hinges on formalizing the currently verbal agreements with ServiceNow for platform access, co-selling, and IP licensing, which is intended to become the primary channel for customer acquisition and scaling [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].

## Revenue & Business Model Path

The revenue path is built on a premium-priced, hybrid subscription model that combines recurring fees with usage-based charges, with target annual contract values (ACVs) starting at $325,000 for the entry-level tier [CHAPTER: revenue-model]. This pricing positions Novaworks significantly above established mid-market players, a bet that customers will pay a premium for the value of an AI-native solution deeply integrated into the ServiceNow platform. The projected unit economics are exceptionally optimistic, with LTV/CAC ratios exceeding 100x, and are predicated on achieving extremely low customer acquisition costs through the unproven ServiceNow co-sell channel [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown]. The model's viability is therefore directly tied to the successful execution of the go-to-market partnership and validation of the premium price point.

## Meta-Analysis: Risks & Opportunities of This Path

Novaworks' strategic path is a high-risk, high-reward play to create a native HCM system of record on the Now Platform. The strategy requires flawless, sequential execution: building a complex, AI-native product from scratch on an accelerated timeline; leveraging this product to formalize a critical co-sell partnership with ServiceNow; and using that partnership to sell a premium-priced solution to enterprise customers. This entire path is built on a foundation of unvalidated, stacked assumptions. The linchpin assumptions that must hold true are the team's ability to execute the complex technical build from a standstill, the successful conversion of verbal agreements with ServiceNow into a formal, favorable partnership for both IP and distribution, and the market's willingness to pay a premium price for a new solution that requires replacing or augmenting a core system of record, as detailed in the *Opportunity Validation* and *Regulatory & Legal Landscape Summary* sections.

The opportunity is strategically compelling for ServiceNow, offering a direct challenge to HCM incumbents like Workday from within its own ecosystem. If successful, Novaworks could achieve rapid scale by leveraging ServiceNow's distribution channels, leading to a valuable acquisition. However, the path is exceptionally fragile. The venture's financial model, with its unrealistic LTV/CAC projections and tight 15-month runway, leaves no margin for error in product development or the 6-9 month enterprise sales cycle [CHAPTER: revenue-model], [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. The dependency on ServiceNow is both the venture's greatest asset and its single point of failure; any shift in ServiceNow's strategy could render the business model unviable. The investment thesis rests on the belief that the experienced founding team can navigate these significant technical, commercial, and partnership risks simultaneously.

## Unit Economics Summary

Novaworks' projected unit economics are exceptionally aggressive and currently unsubstantiated by any operational data. The company forecasts a Customer Acquisition Cost (CAC) that declines to $95,380 and a Lifetime Value (LTV) over $10 million, yielding an LTV/CAC ratio of 105.7x by its third year of operations [CHAPTER: unit-economics]. These figures are entirely **Projected** with very low confidence, as the company is pre-revenue and lacks any pilot data to validate its assumptions. The model's viability hinges on achieving a premium price point starting at a $325,000 annual contract value (ACV), a steep and unexplained 70% decline in CAC over two years, and rapid gross margin expansion from 54% to over 79% [CHAPTER: unit-economics], [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 11]. As a pre-product company, none of these assumptions have been validated, rendering the current model a high-risk hypothesis rather than a credible forecast.

## Financials & Operational Plan

The financial trajectory and operational plan are built on a series of optimistic assumptions that are not internally consistent. The plan requires a $7 million seed investment to fund 15-16 months of operations, with a goal of reaching near-EBITDA breakeven by the end of Year 3 on $13.1 million in revenue [CHAPTER: finance-and-operations], [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 15, 16].

*Source: [CHAPTER: finance-and-operations], [CHAPTER: unit-economics]. All figures are management projections.*

The operational plan is undermined by a significant discrepancy between the stated initial hiring plan of 15-17 employees and the financial model's Year 1 personnel expense, which implies a 47-person headcount [CHAPTER: finance-and-operations], [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown], [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 16]. This inconsistency suggests the financial model is not grounded in a realistic operational plan. Furthermore, the 15-month runway provides a minimal buffer for common early-stage challenges, such as product development delays or a longer-than-expected 6-9 month sales cycle, creating a high risk of premature insolvency if revenue targets are missed [CHAPTER: finance-and-operations], [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].

## Legal & IP Constraints

The venture's operational path is constrained by significant legal and intellectual property risks that directly impact its ability to execute. The most critical constraint is the reliance on an unformalized "verbal agreement" to license core "Skills Intelligence" IP from ServiceNow [CHAPTER: legal-and-ip], [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. This creates an immediate operational bottleneck, as development cannot proceed with certainty until a formal written agreement is executed. The verbal agreement also includes a grant-back clause, which could operationally encumber the R&D team by requiring them to share proprietary improvements back to ServiceNow, potentially limiting the venture's ability to build a defensible, independent IP moat [CHAPTER: legal-and-ip], [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].

Furthermore, the platform's core function—using AI for employment and workforce management—places it in a "high-risk" category under emerging regulations like the EU AI Act [CHAPTER: legal-and-ip], [Cimplifi](https://www.cimplifi.com/resources/the-updated-state-of-ai-regulations-for-2025/?utm_source=openai). This imposes a substantial compliance burden that must be integrated into the product development lifecycle from day one, requiring investment in data governance, transparency, and risk management that can slow down an agile, pre-product team and increase development costs. Finally, the lack of executed IP assignment agreements with founders presents a foundational risk that could disrupt operations and complicate future financing or acquisition events if not rectified immediately upon funding [CHAPTER: legal-and-ip], [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].

## Meta-Analysis: Execution Readiness, Risks & Opportunities

Novaworks' execution readiness is **Weak**. While the venture is led by a highly credible team with exceptional founder-market fit and is targeting a well-timed market opportunity, the operational and financial foundations required to execute its strategy are critically flawed. The plan is built upon an unreliable financial model with unrealistic unit economics and a significant internal inconsistency regarding the Year 1 hiring plan. This disconnect between the strategic vision and the operational budget suggests the company does not yet have a viable plan to get from its current pre-product stage to initial market traction.

The most material operational risks are the direct consequences of this weak foundation. First, the **financial model's unreliability** means the entire plan for resource allocation, hiring, and runway is built on faulty assumptions. Second, the **insufficient runway** of 15 months provides no margin for error against an aggressive timeline that depends on flawless product development and immediate sales success in a 6-9 month enterprise sales cycle. Any delay will likely trigger a cash crisis before key validation milestones are met. Third, the **unformalized ServiceNow IP license** represents an existential operational threat; development could be halted or the venture's core value could be encumbered by the grant-back clause, undermining the entire investment thesis.

In its current state, the venture does not have the necessary resources, constraints, or economic model to support successful execution. The opportunity lies in the team's potential to correct these foundational issues. If the founders can build a credible, bottoms-up operational and financial plan, formalize the critical ServiceNow partnership, and validate their core pricing assumptions, the venture's strong strategic positioning and experienced leadership could be unlocked. However, without these corrections, the current plan is not executable.

## Next Steps and Action Plan

The recommendation to proceed with a strategic investment is contingent upon the successful and timely resolution of critical uncertainties. The following action plan outlines the immediate next steps required to validate core assumptions and de-risk the venture before committing to full-scale development.

# Six T Analysis

# Chapter: 6T Risk Assessment Memorandum

### 1. Executive Risk Summary

**Overall Project Risk Profile**: This is a high-potential venture led by a proven team that is rendered un-investable for the corporate investor in its current form due to a fatal strategic misalignment.

**Top 3 Critical Risks**:

- **Strategic Misalignment (Source: TAM)**: The venture is designed to be built on a competitor's platform (ServiceNow) with the explicit goal of targeting and displacing the investor's (Workday's) own customers, creating a direct and irreconcilable conflict of interest.
- **Technology & IP Encumbrance (Source: Technology, Terms)**: The venture has no proprietary IP and relies on a precarious verbal agreement to license core technology from ServiceNow, which includes a "share-back" clause that would grant a competitor rights to future innovations.
- **Unvalidated Economics & Traction (Source: Traction)**: The venture is pre-product and pre-revenue, with a business model built on what are assessed to be "unrealistic" financial projections, including a 105.7x LTV/CAC ratio, and lacks any validation from independent customers.

**Key Mitigating Strengths**: The venture is led by a highly experienced founding team with a successful entrepreneurial track record and deep domain expertise. They have assembled a strong advisory board of target customers (CHROs) and have correctly identified a large, underserved market segment in the deskless workforce.

**Overall Confidence in Analysis**: High.

The source documents provide clear, consistent evidence of the critical strategic, legal, and commercial risks that make the venture untenable in its current configuration.

**Strategic Recommendation**: **No-Go** on the investment under the current terms and strategy. The venture requires a fundamental strategic pivot away from the competitor's platform to become an investable opportunity for this corporate investor.

**The Core Decision**: The decision is not about the quality of the team or the market opportunity, but whether the founding team is coachable and willing to undertake a significant pivot of their product and go-to-market strategy to align with the investor's ecosystem.

**90-Day De-Risking Plan for Go/No-Go Decision**:

1. **Mandate a Strategic Pivot Plan** (Owner: Project Lead)
2. **Formalize the ServiceNow IP Agreement**

(Owner: Corporate Development)

3. **Secure an Independent Customer Letter of Intent**

(Owner: Project Lead)

### 2. The 6T Risk Matrix

### 3. Deep Dive: Diagnostic Analysis & Recommended Actions

---

#### **Team: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The founding team is a significant asset with proven execution capability, but this strength is undermined by a critical leadership gap in their stated area of differentiation (AI) and a strategic misalignment on exit strategy that creates long-term governance risk. The root cause is a singular focus on the ServiceNow ecosystem, which informs their hiring priorities and potential exit paths, linking directly to the fatal flaw identified in the **TAM** analysis.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Leadership Gap**: The crucial role of Chief Data & AI Officer is listed as "TBD" for a venture positioning itself as "AI-native" \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=3J6cyRLXlRvTJOq2lWu7JkfZYqEh0je8%2F9RPCp63UWk%3D), p. 17\].
  - **Misaligned Incentives**: Founders are explicitly open to being acquired by "ServiceNow, or some other vendor," a direct conflict with the corporate investor's strategic interests \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 8\].
  - **Key Person Dependency**: The venture has a high dependency on its two co-founders, with an imbalanced initial equity split of 67% for the CEO and 28% for the CTO \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 16\].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: While the team is highly capable, their current strategy and incentive structure make them un-investable for this specific corporate investor without a significant pivot and clarification of long-term alignment.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The CEO and CTO's proven entrepreneurial track records and extensive executive network. The high-caliber advisory board of CHROs from major enterprises \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=3J6cyRLXlRvTJOq2lWu7JkfZYqEh0je8%2F9RPCp63UWk%3D), p. 18\].
- **Impact on Project Success**: Significant
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Condition investment on the hiring of a credible Chief Data & AI Officer with a clear equity allocation.
  - **Action 2**: Secure founder agreement on revised exit strategy terms that align with corporate strategic goals, precluding an exit to a direct competitor.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - How coachable is this team, and how willing are they to pivot from a strategy that is deeply integrated into their personal and professional networks?
  - Can we structure the terms to protect our strategic interests if the founders remain committed to an exit path that benefits a competitor?

---

#### **TAM: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The venture's market strategy is fatally flawed from the perspective of the corporate investor (Workday). It is designed to be built on a direct competitor's platform (ServiceNow) with the explicit purpose of displacing the investor's own products in a "WorkDay take out scenario." This fundamental strategic misalignment is the single most critical risk and makes the venture un-investable in its current form.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Direct Competitive Threat**: The venture's plan includes a "WorkDay take out scenario" and aims to displace Workday's own customers \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 29\].
  - **Unsubstantiated Market Size**: The claimed $12 billion Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) is a company-provided estimate that lacks a transparent, bottom-up calculation, creating a high risk that the true market is significantly smaller \[DOC: [Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=ton%2BE4v%2FIj5f5BC7DkWSTATC0FE6RCP%2BLPm9dgDqUUE%3D), p. 1\].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: Investing in this venture would mean directly funding a competitive threat designed to erode the investor's own market share.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The venture's core insight into the needs of the large and underserved deskless workforce is valuable and could be redirected.
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Mandate a strategic pivot to a platform-agnostic approach or one that aligns with the investor's own ecosystem as a prerequisite for any further consideration.
  - **Action 2**: Require a bottoms-up validation of the Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) based on the newly defined target platform and customer segment.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Is there any conceivable strategic rationale for funding the growth of a competitor's platform ecosystem, even for a financial return?
  - What would a viable, non-ServiceNow-dependent go-to-market strategy look like, and is the team capable of executing such a pivot?

---

#### **Technology: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The venture has a high-risk technology profile characterized by a complete lack of proprietary IP, a dependency on an unproven "agentic AI" concept, and a precarious, unformalized verbal IP license from a key partner that encumbers future development. The root cause is the decision to build entirely within the ServiceNow ecosystem, which has led to IP taint concerns and a dependency on ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" IP, linking directly to the **Terms** and **TAM** risks.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Precarious IP License**: The company has only a "verbal agreement" to license "Skills Intelligence" IP from ServiceNow, which includes a clause requiring them to "share back" any modifications, encumbering their own derivative work \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 21\].
  - **No Existing IP**: The company has intentionally created no IP to date due to concerns about "IP taint" from the founders' current employment, meaning it will start with no proprietary assets \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 2, 12\].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The venture lacks a defensible technology moat and its IP position is too uncertain and encumbered to justify an investment at the proposed valuation.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The team's clear vision for a next-generation user experience powered by AI. The CTO's experience in building and scaling technology ventures.
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Mandate the formalization of the ServiceNow IP license into a written contract as a non-negotiable condition for closing the investment.
  - **Action 2**: Require the development of a proof-of-concept to validate the technical feasibility of the core "agentic AI" before committing significant capital.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - What is the venture's value if the "share-back" clause effectively grants ServiceNow ownership of the core innovation?
  - How can we gain confidence that the "agentic AI" concept is a genuine 10x improvement and not just an incremental feature that incumbents can replicate?

---

#### **Traction: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The venture has no tangible market traction. It is a pre-product, pre-revenue company whose business case is supported only by interest from strategically aligned partners and a financial model built on what are assessed to be "unrealistic" and "unsubstantiated" assumptions. The root cause of this is its early stage, but the reliance on a single partner channel (**TAM**) for its economic assumptions (**Traction**) creates an unacceptably high risk.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Unrealistic Projections**: The financial model projects a 105.7x LTV/CAC ratio by Year 3, a figure described as an "extreme outlier" based on an unproven 70% reduction in customer acquisition costs \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=3J6cyRLXlRvTJOq2lWu7JkfZYqEh0je8%2F9RPCp63UWk%3D), p. 11\].
  - **No Independent Validation**: The company has no paying customers, and all "demand" signals come from "customer zero" partners like Bell Canada, who are already part of the target ServiceNow ecosystem and may not represent the broader market \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 8, 19\].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The complete lack of independent validation and the non-credible financial model mean an investment today is a bet on an unproven hypothesis with no margin of safety.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The strong "soft-circled" interest from ServiceNow and Bell Canada can be used to build initial case studies. The high-profile advisory board can facilitate introductions to potential independent pilot customers.
- **Impact on Project Success**: Significant
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Require the company to secure a signed, non-binding Letter of Intent (LOI) from at least one large enterprise customer that is not directly affiliated with the ServiceNow or Bell Canada partnership ecosystem.
  - **Action 2**: Mandate a rebuild of the financial model with defensible, industry-benchmarked assumptions for CAC, churn, and LTV.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - How much of the early partner interest is a genuine commitment to buy versus a strategic move to encourage development on the ServiceNow platform?
  - What is a realistic LTV/CAC for this business, and does the model still work if the ratio is 5-10x instead of 100x?

---

#### **Trends: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The venture is well-aligned with powerful macro trends (AI adoption, platform consolidation, focus on the deskless workforce), but its execution strategy is too fragile to reliably capitalize on them. The core problem is an existential dependency on an unformalized partnership and an unproven core technology, creating a high risk that the venture is both too early and too fragile. This dependency is a direct result of the flawed **TAM** strategy.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Technology immaturity**: The core "agentic AI" is described as the "least proven aspect" of the plan, suggesting the venture may be too early on a technology not yet ready for reliable enterprise use \[CHAPTER: Product & Technology\].
  - **Existential Partnership Dependency**: The venture's success is entirely dependent on a single, unformalized partnership with ServiceNow, which represents a "single point of failure" \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 3\].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: Favorable market timing cannot overcome a flawed and fragile execution strategy, making it likely the venture will fail to capture the opportunity it has identified.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The strong, validated market pull for AI in HR and solutions for the deskless workforce.
- **Impact on Project Success**: Significant
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Commission third-party technical diligence to assess the maturity and enterprise-readiness of "agentic AI" for core HR functions.
  - **Action 2**: Require the development of a credible "Plan B" strategy that reduces the dependency on the ServiceNow channel.
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Are we comfortable making a bet on a core technology that our own diligence suggests is not yet mature?
  - If the ServiceNow partnership sours or fails to deliver, does this business have any other viable path to market?

---

#### **Terms: Diagnostic Deep Dive**

- **A. Core Diagnosis**: The proposed investment terms carry a high degree of risk due to a critical legal encumbrance and an aggressive valuation. The central problem is a verbal, unformalized IP licensing agreement with ServiceNow that includes a "share-back" clause, creating a material legal risk that is not reflected in the pre-product, pre-revenue valuation. This issue is a direct consequence of the flawed **Technology** and **TAM** strategy.
- **B. Supporting Evidence**:
  - **Critical Legal Risk**: The deal has significant "hair" due to a "verbal agreement to utilize the Skills Intelligence of ServiceNow" that "requires sharing of any modifications made to that IP back to ServiceNow," creating a legal and IP nightmare \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 21\].
  - **Aggressive Valuation**: The company is seeking a $18-25 million pre-money valuation while being pre-product and pre-revenue, with its entire development plan contingent on this funding round \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A38%3A45Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A38%3A45Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=8pxd6h0Izw8gvXv3rfhCxlCApoTzrRoAh7swLvObSlg%3D), p. 2\].
- **C. Strategic Implication**: The unresolved legal and IP risks make the current terms unacceptable, as they could severely compromise the venture's long-term value and exit potential.
- **Key Assets to Leverage**: The clean capitalization table and standard founder vesting terms provide a solid foundation for restructuring the deal once the core risks are addressed.
- **Impact on Project Success**: Critical
- **Path Forward: Recommended Actions**:
  - 🎯 **Action 1**: Make the formalization and legal review of the ServiceNow IP agreement a non-negotiable closing condition.
  - **Action 2**: Restructure the investment as a tranched deal or convertible note tied to the achievement of key de-risking milestones (e.g., technical proof-of-concept, independent customer LOI).
- **Key Discussion Points for Decision-Making**:
  - Are we willing to invest in a company where a primary competitor may have rights to its core derivative IP?
  - What is a defensible valuation for this company once the strategic and IP risks are properly accounted for?

---

# Opportunity Validation

## Overview

Novaworks aims to solve the inefficiency and high cost of legacy Human Capital Management (HCM) systems, which burden HR teams with manual tasks and fail to serve the 80% of global workers who are "deskless." The solution is an AI-native HCM platform built entirely on ServiceNow, targeting enterprises seeking to modernize their HR technology. This presents a priority for ServiceNow as it directly extends the Now Platform into a core system of record, enabling a direct competitive challenge to incumbents like Workday and reinforcing the platform's strategic value for enterprise-wide workflow automation. Evidence for the opportunity is rooted in strong market signals for AI in HCM and company-claimed "customer zero" commitments from ServiceNow and Bell Canada, though this direct demand requires verification. The immediate next step is to validate these customer commitments and formalize the partnership while funding the development of a minimum viable product, with the first major milestone being a functional demo in January 2026.

### Key Takeaways

- **Critical Fact 1**: The entire opportunity is predicated on Novaworks building its solution *on* the ServiceNow platform, creating a unique strategic alignment that extends ServiceNow into a core HCM system of record to challenge incumbents like Workday.
- **Critical Fact 2**: The most critical evidence for demand—commitments from "customer zero" partners ServiceNow and Bell Canada—is currently unverified and represents the single most significant assumption that must be validated before committing further resources.

## Risks

- **Execution Risk**: Novaworks is a pre-product, pre-revenue company with no intellectual property built to date. The proposed timeline to deliver a functional Minimum Viable Product (MVP) by early 2026 is aggressive and carries significant technical and operational risk.
- **Validation Risk**: The claimed "customer zero" commitments from major enterprises like ServiceNow and Bell Canada are the primary evidence of problem-solution fit. If these commitments are not formalized or are less substantial than presented, the core validation for the opportunity is undermined.
- **Market Adoption Risk**: The business model requires customers to either replace a core system of record (e.g., Workday) or pay to run a parallel system. This represents a high-friction sales motion with a significant switching cost, and the market's willingness to do so has not been validated beyond the unconfirmed "customer zero" claims.
- **Partnership Dependency**: The go-to-market strategy is entirely dependent on a deep, formalized partnership with ServiceNow for co-selling and distribution. Failure to execute this partnership effectively would leave Novaworks without a viable path to market.

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **Verify "Customer Zero" Commitments**: Obtain formal documentation (e.g., Letter of Intent, signed pilot agreement) within 30 days to confirm the status and scope of the commitments from ServiceNow, Bell Canada, and Ateko. This directly addresses the primary Validation Risk.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Finalize Seed Investment**: Execute legal documentation for the $1M seed investment from ServiceNow Ventures within the next 30 days to provide the necessary operational runway for the validation plan.
- **Formalize Partnership Agreements**: Codify the "Customer Zero" pilot terms, IP licensing for ServiceNow's Skills Intelligence, and the initial framework for a go-to-market partnership. This action targets the Partnership Dependency risk.
- **Establish Joint Governance**: Form a joint steering committee with representatives from ServiceNow’s Employee Workflows business unit and Novaworks leadership to ensure strategic alignment and monitor progress against the validation path.
- **Evaluate Initial MVP**: Assess the limited MVP demo scheduled for the January 2026 ServiceNow Partner Kickoff. This serves as the first major go/no-go checkpoint to validate technical execution and de-risk the Execution Risk.

## Problem Definition & Strategic Fit

### Problem Specification and Impact

Enterprises face significant operational and financial burdens from legacy Human Capital Management (HCM) systems that are inefficient, costly, and ill-equipped for modern workforce demands \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=MpqtKO34Y5fYV%2BsRF9fGQ58pP%2FeoDb6VOnYIn0%2B2sDc%3D), p. unknown\]. These systems create quantifiable drains on productivity and resources. Manual data entry by HR professionals costs an average of $4.86 per instance, and HR teams spend up to 57% of their time on administrative work instead of strategic initiatives [Business Wire — Paycom Reveals Record-High Cost of Manual HR Tasks, Based on EY Study](https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20251015555659/en/Paycom-Reveals-Record-High-Cost-of-Manual-HR-Tasks-Based-on-EY-Study), [Eddy — The Hidden Costs of Manual HR: Why 57% of HR Professionals are Overwhelmed and How Small Businesses Can Fight Back](https://eddy.com/blog/the-hidden-costs-of-manual-hr/). The financial impact is compounded by errors, with each payroll mistake costing an average of $291 to correct [Eddy — The Hidden Costs of Manual HR: Why 57% of HR Professionals are Overwhelmed and How Small Businesses Can Fight Back](https://eddy.com/blog/the-hidden-costs-of-manual-hr/). At a macro level, outdated HR systems result in losses estimated at nearly $1 billion annually in the public sector alone [PR Newswire — Outdated HR Systems Cost Government $1 Billion Annually, New Workday Report Shows](https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/outdated-hr-systems-cost-government-1-billion-annually-new-workday-report-shows-302451828.html).

This problem is particularly acute for the "deskless" workforce—including employees in retail, manufacturing, and logistics—who constitute 80% of the global workforce but have been historically underserved by traditional HCM technology \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=MpqtKO34Y5fYV%2BsRF9fGQ58pP%2FeoDb6VOnYIn0%2B2sDc%3D), p. unknown\], \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=rArOYo0OLKIBidSyA7vWrc1%2B%2Bkjn1n%2F7wuHymfOW9xE%3D), p. unknown\]. These employees require mobile-first, accessible tools that are not typically prioritized by incumbent platforms.

### Current Solutions and Gaps

The current HCM market is fragmented, forcing enterprises to choose between two suboptimal options. On one side, vendors like Rippling and HiBob serve the mid-market but are considered too small to scale with growing companies \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=MpqtKO34Y5fYV%2BsRF9fGQ58pP%2FeoDb6VOnYIn0%2B2sDc%3D), p. unknown\]. On the other side, enterprise incumbents such as Workday and SAP SuccessFactors are expensive to implement and maintain, and their legacy architecture is not inherently designed for an AI-native, agentic operating model \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=MpqtKO34Y5fYV%2BsRF9fGQ58pP%2FeoDb6VOnYIn0%2B2sDc%3D), p. unknown\].

This creates a distinct market gap for an AI-native HCM platform that can both scale to enterprise needs and address the specific requirements of the deskless workforce \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=rArOYo0OLKIBidSyA7vWrc1%2B%2Bkjn1n%2F7wuHymfOW9xE%3D), p. unknown\]. Novaworks proposes to fill this gap by offering a solution that reduces the total cost of ownership and technical complexity by leveraging a unified platform architecture \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=MpqtKO34Y5fYV%2BsRF9fGQ58pP%2FeoDb6VOnYIn0%2B2sDc%3D), p. unknown\].

### Corporate Advantage and Strategic Alignment

Novaworks presents a compelling strategic fit for ServiceNow by directly addressing a core corporate objective: extending the Now Platform into every major enterprise workflow. The opportunity moves beyond a simple partnership, as Novaworks is building its entire AI-native HCM solution *on* the ServiceNow platform \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A43Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A43Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=MpqtKO34Y5fYV%2BsRF9fGQ58pP%2FeoDb6VOnYIn0%2B2sDc%3D), p. unknown\]. This approach provides ServiceNow with a unique and powerful corporate advantage.

The strategic alignment is evident across several dimensions, as detailed in the table below.

Novaworks serves as a proof point for ServiceNow's vision of becoming the "control tower for agentic orchestration for every enterprise" [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Addressing an Underserved Market</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>By targeting the deskless workforce, Novaworks opens a large and historically neglected market segment for the Now Platform, reinforcing ServiceNow's goal of making work better for everyone, not just knowledge workers [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

By supporting Novaworks, ServiceNow can accelerate its strategy to capture the core HCM market, deepen its wallet share within existing enterprise accounts, and reinforce the Now Platform as the central nervous system for modern, AI-powered business operations.

## Market Timing & Catalysts

The opportunity for an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) solution is driven by a convergence of technological maturity, shifting enterprise priorities, and competitive repositioning. The timing is predicated on recent market changes that create a window for a new entrant to challenge incumbents.

### Enabling Factors: The Convergence of AI Maturity and Platform Strategy

The viability of an AI-native HCM platform has been unlocked by two primary factors within the last 24 months: the rapid maturation of generative AI and the strategic evolution of enterprise platforms like ServiceNow.

- **Generative AI Adoption:** The use of generative AI in the workplace has accelerated, with global adoption jumping from 55% in 2023 to 75% in 2024 [GFoundry — 2025 Global Human Capital Trends](https://gfoundry.com/wp-content/uploads/2025/05/DI_2025-Global-Human-Capital-Trends-From-GFoundry.pdf). This widespread adoption has moved AI from a hypothetical advantage to a core business requirement. Novaworks asserts that this technological shift has lowered the barriers to entry for disrupting legacy HCM providers \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Platform-First Enterprise Strategy:** Enterprises are increasingly standardizing on single platforms to improve efficiency and manage AI transformation \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]. ServiceNow's strategic positioning as a "Platform of Platforms" with investments in a unified "Workflow Data Fabric" provides the necessary technical foundation for an integrated, AI-driven application like Novaworks to operate across enterprise data silos \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This aligns with the strategic fit discussed in the *Problem Definition & Strategic Fit* section.

### Urgency Drivers: Market Pull and Incumbent Inefficiency

Demand for AI within HR functions is no longer speculative; it is a stated priority for HR leaders, creating a strong market pull.

- **Prioritized AI Investment:** A 2023 Gartner survey of 349 HR leaders identified "AI in rest of HR technology (including generative AI)" as their most important emerging technology priority \[DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 9\]. This is reinforced by a separate report stating that two-thirds of enterprises are expected to require AI-enabled capabilities in their HCM systems by 2027 [Business Wire — AI Becoming Essential to HCM, ISG Says](https://www.businesswire.com/news/home/20250321088492/en/AI-Becoming-Essential-to-HCM-ISG-Says).
- **Legacy System Gaps:** Novaworks claims that over 70% of mid-market and enterprise HR teams operate with fragmented tech stacks that lack AI-native capabilities \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]. Incumbent solutions from vendors like Workday and SAP are described as expensive and not built to empower a modern AI strategy at scale, creating an opportunity for a challenger built with an AI-first architecture \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Economic Pressure:** A persistent executive mandate to "do more with less" is driving demand for automation that can increase managerial spans of control and lower operating costs, a core component of the Novaworks value proposition \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Competitive Dynamics: A Land Grab for AI Technology

The HCM market is experiencing significant M&A activity, indicating that established players recognize the AI technology gap and are moving to address it through acquisition. This creates both a threat and a validation of the market timing.

- **Incumbent AI Acquisitions:** In August and September 2025, market leader Workday acquired three separate AI firms (Flowise, Paradox, and Sana) to integrate AI into its platform [WorldatWork — Recent HR Software Acquisitions Point to More AI-Focused Future](https://worldatwork.org/publications/workspan-daily/recent-hr-software-acquisitions-point-to-more-ai-focused-future). This reactive "buy" strategy from incumbents highlights the urgency and validates the importance of AI capabilities, while also creating a window for a natively built solution to differentiate itself from bolted-on technologies.
- **High-Value Market Consolidation:** The HCM sector has seen major transactions, including Thoma Bravo's $12.3 billion acquisition of Dayforce in August 2025 and ADP's acquisition of WorkForce Software in October 2024 [Reuters — Thoma Bravo to buy Dayforce in $12.3 billion deal](https://www.reuters.com/legal/transactional/thoma-bravo-buy-dayforce-123-billion-deal-2025-08-21/), [Reuters — ADP raises annual revenue growth forecast following WorkForce Software acquisition](https://www.reuters.com/technology/adp-raises-annual-revenue-growth-forecast-following-workforce-software-2024-10-30/). This activity signals strong investor confidence and high strategic value in the market.

### Window of Opportunity Assessment

The confluence of market-ready AI technology, clear customer demand, and reactive M&A from incumbents creates a time-sensitive window of opportunity.

Waiting a year would likely result in a more crowded market where incumbents have made further progress in integrating their acquired AI technologies, potentially diminishing the "AI-native" differentiation. The current moment presents a clear opportunity to address validated market demand before the competitive landscape solidifies.

## Demand Signals & Validation Evidence

Evidence for customer demand for an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) solution is supported by strong indirect market signals, though direct demand for Novaworks' specific product remains based on company-reported claims that require validation. The most significant indicators are the broad, technology-driven shifts in the HCM market and preliminary interest from strategic partners.

### Direct and Indirect Demand Signals

The available evidence for demand can be categorized from direct, company-specific signals to broader, independently verified market trends.

Reuters
