</table>

### Critical Assumptions and Validation Gaps

While market tailwinds are strong, Novaworks' success depends on several critical, unverified assumptions. Validating these points, as outlined in the *Resource Requirements & Validation Path* section, represents the most immediate priority.

1. **Nature of "Customer Zero" Commitments**: The most critical assumption is the claim that ServiceNow and Bell Canada will serve as initial customers. The diligence questionnaire states both are Workday customers, making their commitment a powerful validation signal for a "take out" or augmentation strategy \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. However, the current evidence is entirely company-reported. The formal status of these agreements—whether they are verbal commitments, letters of intent, or signed contracts—is unknown and must be verified.

2. **Willingness to Replace or Augment Core HCM**: Novaworks acknowledges that its business model requires customers to either replace their existing HCM or pay to run Novaworks' system in parallel \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The "customer zero" commitments are the primary evidence for this willingness, but without independent validation, the readiness of the broader market to incur the cost and complexity of this change remains a significant unknown.

3. **Validated Demand from Deskless Workers**: The company's focus on the deskless workforce is a key part of its strategy, citing that this segment comprises 80% of the global workforce \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]. While the market size is substantial, there is a gap in independent evidence confirming that this segment has a specific, urgent need for an *AI-native* HCM solution that existing platforms fail to address. The claim that 44% of these workers expect better technology is a company assertion requiring external validation \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\].

## Resource Requirements & Validation Path

To de-risk the opportunity, Novaworks must validate its core assumptions through a phased approach focused on technical execution, partnership formalization, and initial customer adoption. The company has outlined a validation path tied to key industry events, requiring a $7 million seed investment to fund operations for 15 months \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 15\].

### Critical Assumptions for Validation

The success of Novaworks hinges on three primary assumptions that require immediate testing, directly addressing the gaps identified in the *Demand Signals & Validation Evidence* section:

1. **Market Adoption:** That target customers are willing to either replace their existing Human Capital Management (HCM) systems or adopt Novaworks as a supplementary AI-driven solution \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 3\].
2. **Strategic Partnership:** That a formal partnership with ServiceNow can be secured, including tangible co-sell and co-market commitments that provide a viable go-to-market channel \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 3\].
3. **Technical Execution:** That the company can develop and deliver a Minimum Viable Product (MVP) on an accelerated timeline, given that no intellectual property has been built to date due to potential conflicts with the founders' prior employment \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 13\].

### Proposed Validation Path and Milestones

Novaworks proposes a three-phase validation plan designed to test its core assumptions and achieve problem-solution fit before scaling.

Develop marketing and sales materials for the launch at ServiceNow's Knowledge event in May [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. 14, 26].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Phase 3: Broader Demand Validation</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>June 2026 – Sep 2026</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Objective:</strong> Convert market interest from the launch into tangible customer commitments. br <strong>Activities:</strong> Leverage leads from the Knowledge event to recruit and sign 7-10 design partners. This phase will test the broader value proposition and sales motion with prospective customers [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. 16].</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

### Resource Requirements

The validation plan is contingent upon securing the requested seed funding.

- **Funding:** A $7 million seed round is required to provide a 15-month operational runway \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 15\]. The company reports soft-circled commitments totaling $4-5 million from ServiceNow Ventures, BCE, and an SPV \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 16\].
- **Personnel:** The initial team will consist of 4-5 US-based employees, one employee in Dubai, and 10 in India. The company plans to use contractors to augment the engineering team to meet MVP deadlines \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 9\].
- **Budget Allocation:** The Year 1 budget allocates $4.1 million for FTE expenses, with a primary focus on product development (56% for R&D) and a secondary focus on initial go-to-market preparations (44% for Sales & G&A) \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 15\].

### Success Metrics and Go/No-Go Criteria

Clear metrics are necessary at each stage to guide the decision to proceed, pivot, or terminate the initiative.

## Strategic Options & Next Steps

Based on Novaworks’ pre-product status and its foundational strategy of building on the ServiceNow platform, the primary strategic decision is not a conventional build-versus-buy analysis but rather defining the optimal structure and timeline for engagement. The company’s plan is inherently a partnership, making the key variables the depth of integration, the level of investment, and the path to a potential future acquisition.

### Evaluation of Strategic Options

Three primary strategic paths exist for engaging with Novaworks. The analysis below evaluates each option based on speed to market, strategic alignment, and resource commitment.

WorldatWork.

\- **Execution Risk:** As a pre-product company, Novaworks carries significant execution risk until it delivers a functional MVP and secures design partners. br- **Limited Control:** ServiceNow will have influence as an investor and partner but not direct control over the product roadmap or operational execution.

Partnership (Recommended)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Proceed with the planned $1M seed investment and formalize a multi-faceted partnership covering technology, go-to-market (GTM), and a "Customer Zero" pilot.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>- <strong>Fastest Path to Validation:</strong> Leverages an external, dedicated team to build a needed solution on the Now Platform, accelerating time-to-market. br- <strong>Capital Efficient:</strong> Uses venture funding to de-risk product development before committing greater internal resources or acquisition capital. br- <strong>Strong Alignment:</strong> The Novaworks roadmap and GTM strategy are explicitly designed around ServiceNow, targeting underpenetrated HRSD customers and planning for combined SKUs [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-<em>Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. br- </em><strong><em>M&amp;A Optionality:</em></strong><em> Establishes a clear path to a potential future acquisition, a stated goal of the Novaworks founders [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW</em>-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]. overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p></p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Option 2: Internal Build</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Allocate internal resources to develop a competing AI-native HCM solution on the Now Platform.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>- <strong>Full Control:</strong> Provides complete control over product development, roadmap, and IP. br- <strong>Direct Integration:</strong> Ensures the solution is built from the ground up to align perfectly with ServiceNow’s architecture and strategic priorities.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Acquire Novaworks at its current pre-product, pre-revenue stage.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>- <strong>Secure Team &amp; Vision:</strong> Immediately secures the founding team and their strategic vision for an AI-native HCM.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>- <strong>Premature Valuation:</strong> Acquiring a company with no product or revenue presents a high-risk valuation challenge. br- <strong>Integration Overhead:</strong> The immediate overhead of integrating a pre-product team could disrupt both Novaworks’ focus and internal ServiceNow teams. br- <strong>Stifles Validation:</strong> Removes the market validation pressure that comes from operating as an independent, venture-backed startup.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

The recommended path is **Option 1: Strategic Investment & Partnership**. This approach provides the most balanced risk-reward profile, allowing ServiceNow to validate the opportunity with minimal initial capital while securing a strategic foothold and maintaining future acquisition as a viable outcome.

### Recommended Next Steps & Validation Path

To execute the recommended strategy, a series of immediate actions and clear validation milestones are required. The Employee Workflows business unit should lead the engagement, with close collaboration from ServiceNow Ventures. This path directly corresponds to the validation plan detailed in the *Resource Requirements & Validation Path* section.

## Claims

 1. Legacy HCM systems create significant operational burdens, with HR teams spending up to 57% of their time on administrative work.
 2. The "deskless" workforce constitutes 80% of the global workforce and is historically underserved by HCM technology.
 3. Novaworks is building its entire AI-native HCM solution on the ServiceNow platform to extend it into a core system of record.
 4. Global adoption of generative AI in the workplace has accelerated from 55% in 2023 to 75% in 2024.
 5. Two-thirds of enterprises are expected to require AI-enabled capabilities in their HCM systems by 2027.
 6. Novaworks claims that ServiceNow and Bell Canada, both current Workday customers, have agreed to serve as "customer zero."
 7. The company is seeking a $7 million seed investment to provide a 15-month operational runway.
 8. Novaworks has no intellectual property built to date due to potential conflicts with founders' prior employment.
 9. The company's validation plan targets the delivery of a limited MVP by January 2026 and a full MVP by May 2026.
10. The recommended strategic path for ServiceNow is to make a $1M seed investment and formalize a multi-faceted partnership.

# Product and Technology

## Overview

Novaworks is building an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform on ServiceNow, centered around a conversational "super agent" to automate HR workflows, specifically targeting the deskless workforce. The core innovation is its agentic architecture, which aims to provide a unified, proactive user experience, contrasting with legacy systems that have merely added AI features. The venture plans to leverage ServiceNow's core platform, AI/data infrastructure, and a verbal agreement for its Skills Intelligence IP, capitalizing on the founding team's deep expertise with the ecosystem. Key technical uncertainties include the complex orchestration of a multi-cloud architecture, ensuring robust data security for sensitive HR information, and achieving reliable performance at scale. A 20-week, three-phase validation plan is proposed to test these core assumptions, starting with a proof-of-concept for the AI agent before committing to full development.

### Key Takeaways

- **Critical Fact 1**: The entire strategy is built on native integration with the ServiceNow platform, leveraging its infrastructure, AI components, and go-to-market channels. This deep alignment is both its greatest strength and most critical dependency.
- **Critical Fact 2**: The project is pre-product and pre-code. Success hinges entirely on the team's ability to execute a complex technical orchestration of multiple systems (ServiceNow, public cloud, third-party LLMs) on an aggressive 15-month timeline.

## Risks

- **Execution Risk**: The team is starting from a complete standstill and must integrate multiple complex systems—including the Now Platform, a public cloud, commercial LLMs, and a vector database—into a reliable, enterprise-grade product on a highly accelerated timeline.
- **Partnership Dependency**: The venture's technical and commercial viability is critically dependent on formalizing its strategic partnership with ServiceNow. This includes co-sell agreements and a definitive license for the Skills Intelligence IP, which is currently based only on a verbal agreement.
- **Data Security and Compliance**: Using autonomous AI agents and third-party LLMs to process highly sensitive employee data creates significant security, privacy, and regulatory compliance risks that are challenging to mitigate in a multi-cloud environment.
- **Performance at Scale**: The "super agent" value proposition requires consistent, low-latency performance. The complex, multi-step workflows involving external LLMs could introduce performance bottlenecks and unpredictable API costs as the user base grows.

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **Formalize ServiceNow Partnership**: Obtain a signed Letter of Intent or Term Sheet from ServiceNow that outlines the specific terms of the co-sell agreement and the non-exclusive license for its Skills Intelligence IP to convert the verbal agreement into a formal commitment.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Execute Phase 1 PoC**: Fund and execute the 6-week Proof of Concept for the core agentic logic, as defined in the Technical Validation Strategy, to test the primary technical assumption before committing further resources to integration and development.
- **Develop Security Protocol**: Create a detailed data governance and security protocol document specifying how Personally Identifiable Information (PII) will be handled, segregated, and protected across the multi-cloud architecture, with a specific focus on data flows to and from third-party LLMs.
- **Model Latency and Cost**: Conduct a preliminary technical analysis to model the expected end-to-end latency and API costs for the 3-5 most common user workflows at scales of 1,000 and 10,000 concurrent users to assess scalability risks early.

## Solution Scope & Architecture

Novaworks is developing an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform built on ServiceNow.

The solution is designed to automate HR workflows and provide a unified, conversational interface for employees, with a specific focus on the historically underserved deskless workforce \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=J1HU%2BCsn%2BiROfGF6cR1mZKLBHUbrBbGLb8%2FlUl%2FxdrY%3D), p. unknown\].

### Core Functionality

The platform's core function is to serve as a comprehensive HCM system covering the entire employee lifecycle, from hiring to retirement. It aims to replace or augment legacy HCM systems by using an "agentic" architecture, where AI agents proactively and reactively manage HR tasks \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=J1HU%2BCsn%2BiROfGF6cR1mZKLBHUbrBbGLb8%2FlUl%2FxdrY%3D), p. unknown\]. The central feature is a "super agent," a voice-enabled, conversational assistant designed to provide a single point of contact for any employee interaction or task, similar to a Siri-like experience \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=J1HU%2BCsn%2BiROfGF6cR1mZKLBHUbrBbGLb8%2FlUl%2FxdrY%3D), p. unknown\].

For employees, the system is intended to deliver hyper-personalized tools, notifications, and support. For managers, it aims to increase operational efficiency and expand their span of control through automation \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=J1HU%2BCsn%2BiROfGF6cR1mZKLBHUbrBbGLb8%2FlUl%2FxdrY%3D), p. unknown\]. The initial target users are exemplified by "Maria," a warehouse manager, and "James," a new machine operator, highlighting the focus on non-office-based roles \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=Mjr8if31ZXCPAPzuxAKO4SvtAW7F0T0rXiIsDmNjBwo%3D), p. unknown\].

### Technical Architecture

The Novaworks solution is architected as a multi-tenant, platform-independent set of capabilities that are initially deployed on the ServiceNow platform and a public cloud (AWS or Azure) \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=Mjr8if31ZXCPAPzuxAKO4SvtAW7F0T0rXiIsDmNjBwo%3D), p. unknown\]. The architecture consists of four primary layers:

1. **Frontend & User Interface**: The user-facing components are built within ServiceNow, using its HR Workspace and EC Pro modules, alongside custom components. A "Nova Chat Integrations" module provides the conversational interface \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=Mjr8if31ZXCPAPzuxAKO4SvtAW7F0T0rXiIsDmNjBwo%3D), p. unknown\].
2. **AI & Agent Layer (Nova GPT)**: This layer orchestrates the AI functionality. It uses an agentic framework, explicitly mentioning the use of LangChain, a common open-source toolkit for developing applications powered by large language models (LLMs) \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=J1HU%2BCsn%2BiROfGF6cR1mZKLBHUbrBbGLb8%2FlUl%2FxdrY%3D), p. unknown\], [Medium](https://medium.com/@admin_52806/the-top-5-frameworks-driving-the-agentic-ai-revolution-in-2025-ad9006e17e09). This layer combines commercial LLMs with a proprietary "Nova SLM" (Small Language Model) \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=Mjr8if31ZXCPAPzuxAKO4SvtAW7F0T0rXiIsDmNjBwo%3D), p. unknown\].
3. **Data & Knowledge Layer (Nova Codex)**: This is a serverless data lakehouse that ingests public, partner, and customer data. It uses custom transformers to process and store this information in a vector database, which is essential for providing context to the AI agents \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=Mjr8if31ZXCPAPzuxAKO4SvtAW7F0T0rXiIsDmNjBwo%3D), p. unknown\].
4. **Integration Layer**: An "Integration Hub" and "Workflow Data Fabric" connect the platform to external systems for functions such as payroll, background checks, and e-signatures \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=Mjr8if31ZXCPAPzuxAKO4SvtAW7F0T0rXiIsDmNjBwo%3D), p. unknown\].

### Scope Boundaries

The product is planned for a phased rollout over five years, starting with foundational HR capabilities and progressively adding advanced talent management modules and vertical-specific specializations. The initial Minimum Viable Product (MVP) is focused on core administrative and workforce management functions, while functions like payroll and benefits administration are planned as partner integrations \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A51Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A51Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=J1HU%2BCsn%2BiROfGF6cR1mZKLBHUbrBbGLb8%2FlUl%2FxdrY%3D), p. unknown\].

<table class="border-collapse w-full" style="min-width: 75px;">
<colgroup><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"></colgroup><tbody><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Capability Area</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Year 1–2 Scope (MVP &amp; Transaction Management; Position and Org Management.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Expansion of existing capabilities for specific industries.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Workforce Management</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Time &amp; Retail; Telecommunications.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Manufacturing; Healthcare; Technology.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Compliance &amp; </table>

*Source: \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]*

### Innovation Elements

The primary innovation claimed by Novaworks is not a single new technology but the synthesis of existing technologies into an "AI-native" HCM platform, as opposed to a legacy system with AI features added on. Key innovative elements include:

- **Agentic Architecture**: The solution is designed around autonomous AI agents that can execute complex, multi-step HR workflows, aiming to reduce manual intervention and increase manager efficiency \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Deskless Workforce Focus**: The product is purpose-built for the needs of frontline workers, a segment that comprises 80% of the global workforce but has been historically underserved by traditional HCM systems \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Unified "Super Agent" Experience**: Consolidating all employee interactions into a single, voice-enabled conversational interface is a key differentiator from fragmented, multi-application HR tech stacks \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Native ServiceNow Integration**: By building on the ServiceNow platform, Novaworks intends to use its security, low-code customization capabilities, and "Workflow Data Fabric" to accelerate deployment and connect siloed enterprise data \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This deep integration is detailed further in the Corporate Capability Alignment section.

### User Experience

The intended user experience centers on simplicity and accessibility, driven by the conversational "super agent." For an employee, this means interacting with a single AI assistant for tasks ranging from requesting time off to inquiring about career development opportunities. For a manager, the experience is designed to automate routine administrative work, such as onboarding new hires or approving schedules, allowing them to focus on higher-value management activities \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]. The platform aims to provide a "hyper personalized" experience for each employee, delivering proactive notifications and just-in-time support through their preferred communication channels \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

## Technology Feasibility & Maturity

The technical feasibility of Novaworks' proposed solution is assessed as **Medium confidence**. While the core technologies are commercially available and maturing rapidly, significant execution risk exists in orchestrating these components into a reliable, secure, and scalable enterprise-grade Human Capital Management (HCM) platform. The company is not assuming any technical breakthroughs are required; success depends on engineering execution rather than fundamental research and development.

### Technology Readiness and Precedents

Novaworks’ technical approach relies on a combination of mature, commercially available technologies. The core concept of using agentic AI to automate complex HR workflows is well-established, with major enterprise software providers, including ServiceNow, already deploying AI agents in their HR service delivery products [Deel](https://www.deel.com/blog/agentic-ai-tools-for-hr). The broader market trend validates that agentic systems are a viable and increasingly adopted solution for enhancing HR efficiency and workforce planning [Prismforce](https://prismforce.com/blog/agentic-ai-in-hr-the-complete-guide), [Qandle](https://www.qandle.com/blog/how-hr-must-adapt-to-agentic-ai-in-the-workplace/).

The company’s plan to build its agent layer using "publicly available LLMs" and open-source toolkits like LangChain is a standard industry practice \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. These foundational frameworks are sufficiently mature for developing multi-agent systems, providing the necessary components for building the proposed architecture [Blockchain Council](https://www.blockchain-council.org/ai/agentic-ai-tools-frameworks/).

The most significant enabler is the decision to build on the ServiceNow platform. This choice de-risks multiple technical domains by providing a secure, enterprise-grade foundation for workflow automation, user interface development, and data management through its Workflow Data Fabric \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]. This approach allows Novaworks to focus on its core value proposition—the AI-native HCM application logic—rather than building foundational infrastructure.

### Key Technical Risks and Challenges

Despite the availability of core technologies, Novaworks faces three primary technical risks that will determine its ability to deliver a functional and competitive product. A staged approach to validate these assumptions is outlined in the Technical Validation Strategy section.

1. **Complex System Orchestration:** The primary technical challenge is not in the individual components but in their integration and orchestration. The proposed architecture spans the ServiceNow cloud and a public cloud (AWS or Azure) for its data lakehouse, connecting a custom front-end, multiple AI models (commercial LLM and a custom "Nova SLM"), and a vector database via an agent layer \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. unknown\]. Engineering a reliable, low-latency, and seamless "super agent" experience from these disparate parts is a substantial undertaking.
2. **Data Governance and Security:** As an HCM system of record, the platform will handle highly sensitive employee data. Ensuring robust data privacy, security, and regulatory compliance across a multi-cloud architecture that uses third-party LLMs is a critical challenge. While the company plans a "Nova HR Codex for Global Compliance," the implementation of effective governance and risk mitigation for autonomous AI agents remains a significant hurdle that requires specialized frameworks \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], [arXiv](https://arxiv.org/abs/2510.15739).
3. **Performance and Scalability:** The value proposition of delivering a "hyper personalized" experience to every employee requires consistent, low-latency performance at scale \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The reliance on external commercial LLMs and complex, multi-step agentic workflows could introduce performance bottlenecks and unpredictable costs as the user base grows to the target enterprise segments of over 20,000 full-time employees \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Required Enablers and Dependencies

The successful development of the Novaworks platform is contingent on the integration and performance of several key external technologies and platforms. The company's strategy mitigates risk by using established services rather than developing foundational technology from scratch.

The key dependency is the ability to achieve deep, performant integration with ServiceNow's APIs and data models.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Third-Party Data Integration</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The platform's "Integration Hub" must connect to external enterprise systems for functions like payroll, background checks, and e-signatures to deliver an end-to-end HCM experience [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>While conceptually sound, this requires significant implementation effort. Success is dependent on the availability, reliability, and consistency of APIs from a wide range of third-party vendors.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

## Corporate Capability Alignment

Novaworks' strategy demonstrates a high degree of alignment with ServiceNow's existing corporate capabilities, leveraging the Now Platform as its foundational technology. The venture is designed to function as a native extension of ServiceNow's ecosystem rather than a standalone product, which creates significant technical and go-to-market advantages.

### Existing Assets and Platform Leverage

The core of Novaworks' technical strategy is its construction upon the ServiceNow platform, which provides immediate access to a secure, scalable, and enterprise-ready infrastructure \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This approach allows Novaworks to bypass foundational development and focus on building its AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) application layer.

Novaworks plans to use several key ServiceNow assets:

- **Core Platform Services**: The solution will be built using ServiceNow's low-code development platform and will integrate with existing components like HR Workspace and EC Pro \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 10\]. This native integration is intended to reduce deployment complexity for customers already within the ServiceNow ecosystem \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **AI and Data Infrastructure**: The architecture explicitly incorporates ServiceNow's strategic data and AI components, including the Workflow Data Fabric and RaptorDB, to connect disparate enterprise data sources for its AI agents \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The solution is also designed to operate within ServiceNow's AI governance frameworks, such as the AI Control Tower and AI Agent Fabric, which provide orchestration and management for all agents on the platform \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 30, 31\].
- **Intellectual Property**: Novaworks has a verbal agreement to use ServiceNow's Skills Intelligence IP through a non-exclusive license, which provides a critical technology component and accelerates the development of its talent management capabilities \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Internal Expertise and Business Unit Fit

The venture shows strong alignment with ServiceNow's internal talent and strategic business focus. The Novaworks founding team has deep institutional knowledge of the ServiceNow platform, evidenced by their approved conflict of interest filings \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This is further reinforced by an advisory board that includes several current and former ServiceNow executives, providing access to strategic guidance and internal networks \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 18\].

From a business perspective, Novaworks fits directly into the HR Service Delivery (HRSD) business unit's strategy. The go-to-market plan targets existing ServiceNow HRSD customers, particularly in the underpenetrated commercial segment \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 11\]. The designation of ServiceNow as "customer zero" creates an ideal environment for co-development, rapid feedback, and internal validation before a broader market launch \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This aligns with ServiceNow's broader role in the HR technology market, where its platform serves as a central hub for integrating various HR functions [ERP.Today](https://erp.today/servicenows-critical-role-in-todays-hr-tech-market/).

### Capability Gaps and Partnership Strategy

Novaworks' primary capability gap is that the product is not yet built, a deliberate decision to avoid intellectual property contamination while the founders were still employed at ServiceNow \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This presents an execution risk, which is addressed in the Implementation Roadmap & Resources section.

The company's technology strategy relies on a sensible build-versus-buy approach. While building the core HCM application and agentic workflows on the Now Platform, Novaworks plans to use external, best-of-breed technologies for commodity components. This includes using publicly available Large Language Models (LLMs) and open-source agent development frameworks like LangChain, which is a standard tool for building AI agents that can reason through tasks \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], [Medium](https://medium.com/@admin_52806/the-top-5-frameworks-driving-the-agentic-ai-revolution-in-2025-ad9006e17e09).

The most critical dependency is the formalization of the strategic partnership with ServiceNow. Success requires establishing co-sell and co-marketing agreements and potentially developing a combined SKU to simplify procurement for customers \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 14\]. While this is primarily a business development activity, it is fundamental to realizing the technical and product vision.

### Summary of Alignment

[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown]</p></td></tr></tbody>

## Implementation Roadmap & Resources

Novaworks presents a phased implementation plan designed to progress from its current pre-product status to a commercially scaled solution over approximately 15 months, contingent on securing a $7M seed round \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 15\]. The roadmap prioritizes rapid development to meet key industry event deadlines, followed by a pilot program with committed design partners before broader market expansion. The strategy is predicated on an aggressive timeline, starting development from a complete standstill due to intellectual property restrictions that prevent any code creation until after funding is secured and founders have formally separated from ServiceNow \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Development Phases and Timeline

The company has defined a four-phase path from initial prototype to commercial scaling. This approach includes distinct deliverables and decision gates at each stage to manage risk and validate progress before committing further resources. The initial timeline is accelerated, a pace which is supported by current industry capabilities in rapid AI prototyping that can shorten development cycles from months to weeks [Speed MVPs](https://speedmvps.com/rapid-ai-prototyping), [Hypermode](https://hypermode.com/blog/ai-native-architectures-rapid-iteration-development).

Prepare for a Series A funding round to support upmarket expansion [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Key performance indicators (e.g., adoption, retention) support further investment in growth.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

### Resource Allocation

Novaworks plans a lean initial structure focused on product development, with a clear strategy to shift investment toward go-to-market functions as the product matures.

- **Initial Team Structure**: At launch, the team will consist of 4-5 US-based employees, one executive in Dubai, and a 10-person engineering team in India, augmented by contractors as needed \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The total projected headcount for the first year is 47 \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*, p. 16\].
- **Phased Investment**: The allocation of the $4.1M Year 1 FTE expense heavily favors development, with 56% dedicated to R&D. In Year 2, the allocation shifts, with 52% of the $5.8M FTE expense directed to Sales & G&A, reflecting the transition from building the product to selling it \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 15\].
- **Technology Resources**: The technical architecture relies on public cloud infrastructure (AWS or Azure), open-source AI development toolkits like LangChain, and commercial Large Language Models (LLMs) \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*, p. 10\].

### Critical Dependencies

The roadmap's success hinges on several key internal and external factors that must be secured for the plan to remain viable.

- **Funding**: The entire implementation plan is contingent on the successful close of the $7M seed round \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 15\].
- **Strategic Partnerships**: Formalizing the partnership with ServiceNow is the most critical dependency. This includes finalizing terms for co-sell and co-market activities and securing a definitive, non-exclusive license for ServiceNow's Skills Intelligence IP, which is currently based on a verbal agreement \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Design Partner Commitment**: The pilot phase relies on the active participation of "customer zero" partners—ServiceNow, Bell Canada, and Ateko—to provide essential feedback for product iteration \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 14\].

### Scale Considerations

Novaworks' strategy for scaling is built into its product architecture and operational planning. The company intends to grow efficiently before pursuing a larger Series A round to fund a more aggressive expansion.

- **Architectural Scalability**: The solution is designed to serve mid-market customers with an off-the-shelf product while enabling rapid customization for larger enterprises through the ServiceNow low-code development platform \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Operational Scaling**: The company plans to maintain a lean organization, scaling the customer success and sales teams only after the product and initial demand are validated \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. Headcount is projected to grow modestly from 47 to 53 between Year 1 and Year 2, prioritizing capital efficiency \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*, p. 16\].
- **Future Funding for Scale**: Management explicitly states the intention to raise a Series A round after achieving product-market fit to fund the expansion into the large enterprise segment and challenge incumbent vendors like Workday \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

## Technical Validation Strategy

To de-risk the technical development of Novaworks' platform, a staged validation strategy is proposed. This approach prioritizes testing the most critical technical assumptions with minimal resource expenditure before committing to full-scale development, which is essential for a pre-product company \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 13\]. The strategy emphasizes rapid prototyping, a method proven to shorten development cycles and validate concepts quickly [SpeedMVPs](https://speedmvps.com/rapid-ai-prototyping), [Janea Systems](https://www.janeasystems.com/blog/ai-project-failure-rapid-prototyping-solution).

### Key Technical Assumptions

The viability of the Novaworks solution depends on four core technical hypotheses derived from its proposed architecture \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 10\]. These must be validated empirically.

1. **Agentic AI Performance:** The central assumption is that an AI agent built using open-source frameworks like LangChain can reliably orchestrate complex, multi-step Human Capital Management (HCM) workflows (e.g., new hire onboarding, performance reviews) with high accuracy and minimal human intervention \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 24\].
2. **ServiceNow Platform Integration:** The solution's value is predicated on its ability to deeply integrate with the ServiceNow platform. It must leverage core components like EC Pro and the Workflow Data Fabric without introducing performance bottlenecks or compromising the stability of the host environment \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 10\].
3. **LLM Accuracy and Compliance:** The use of commercial Large Language Models (LLMs) for a regulated function like HR introduces risk. The assumption is that these models can be constrained through prompt engineering and retrieval-augmented generation (RAG) to provide factually correct, compliant, and non-hallucinatory responses suitable for an enterprise context.
4. **Data Security and Multi-Tenancy:** The proposed multi-tenant architecture must ensure strict data segregation between customers to meet enterprise security and privacy standards (e.g., GDPR, CCPA) \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 10\].

### Staged Validation Approach

A three-phase approach is recommended to systematically test these assumptions and accelerate learning, consistent with modern AI development practices that favor rapid iteration [Hypermode](https://hypermode.com/blog/ai-native-architectures-rapid-iteration-development).

- **Phase 1: Proof of Concept (PoC) — Core Agentic Logic (Weeks 1-6):** This phase focuses exclusively on the highest-risk element: the AI agent's ability to execute a core HCM workflow. The PoC will be a standalone service, using mock data to isolate and validate the agent's reasoning and task-completion capabilities.
- **Phase 2: Functional Prototype — ServiceNow Integration (Weeks 7-12):** The validated PoC agent will be integrated into a ServiceNow developer instance. This phase will test the technical feasibility of the agent reading from and writing to ServiceNow, validating the core integration hypothesis.
- **Phase 3: Limited Pilot — Design Partner Deployment (Weeks 13-20):** The functional prototype will be deployed in a sandboxed environment for a designated design partner, such as Bell Canada or Ateko \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 14\]. This phase will test the solution against real-world use cases and data (anonymized where necessary) to validate performance and utility.

### Validation Experiments and Success Metrics

The following table outlines specific experiments, metrics, and timelines for the validation strategy.

### Risk Mitigation and Learning Velocity

This staged strategy is designed to mitigate technical risk by front-loading the validation of the most novel and uncertain architectural components. Each phase concludes with a go/no-go decision point, minimizing resource commitment if a core assumption proves invalid. For instance, if the Phase 1 PoC fails to achieve a 90% task completion rate, the project would require a significant architectural review before proceeding, preventing wasted effort on integration. This "fail fast" approach prioritizes learning velocity, ensuring that the development roadmap is continuously informed by empirical evidence rather than static plans.

## Claims

 1. Novaworks is developing an AI-native HCM platform on ServiceNow using an agentic architecture.
 2. The solution's primary user interface is a voice-enabled, conversational "super agent."
 3. The initial target market is the deskless workforce in industries like transportation, retail, and telecommunications.
 4. The technical architecture is a multi-tenant system spanning ServiceNow and a public cloud such as AWS or Azure.
 5. The platform relies on commercial LLMs, an open-source framework (LangChain), and a proprietary Small Language Model.
 6. The entire implementation plan is contingent on securing a $7M seed funding round.
 7. The company has a verbal agreement to use ServiceNow's Skills Intelligence IP via a non-exclusive license.
 8. Development is starting from zero code due to intellectual property restrictions on the founders.
 9. The initial team will consist of 47 employees in the first year, with 56% of FTE expense dedicated to R&D.
10. A three-phase, 20-week technical validation plan is proposed to de-risk core assumptions before full-scale development.

# Market Research

## Overview

The realistic market opportunity is a niche within the $34.1 billion Human Capital Management (HCM) market, specifically targeting mid-sized ServiceNow customers with deskless workforces. While the overall market is large, the venture's $12 billion serviceable addressable market (SAM) estimate is a low-confidence company claim lacking a transparent methodology. Market dynamics are favorable, driven by AI-led modernization and a focus on the historically underserved deskless segment, creating an opportune time for entry. The competitive landscape is intense, featuring large incumbents like Workday and SAP, but the venture aims to differentiate with an AI-native solution built on the ServiceNow platform. The most critical evidence needed is validation that customers are willing to bear the high costs and disruption of replacing or augmenting their core HCM systems, which can be tested through paid pilot programs and direct customer interviews.

### Key Takeaways

- **Large but Unverified Niche**: The overall HCM market is large and growing ($34.1B), but the venture's $12B serviceable market for the deskless workforce is an unverified, low-confidence company claim that requires a detailed, bottom-up validation.
- **Strategic Conflict**: The core go-to-market strategy relies on a partnership with ServiceNow, a direct competitor to Workday, creating a fundamental strategic misalignment and a single point of failure risk for the internal venture.

## Risks

- **Unsubstantiated Market Size**: The $12B Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM) is a company-provided estimate without a transparent, bottom-up calculation, creating a high risk that the true market opportunity is significantly smaller.
- **Platform Dependency**: The entire go-to-market strategy hinges on a currently informal partnership with ServiceNow, a direct competitor. This creates a critical dependency and a single point of failure if the relationship terms change or are not formalized.
- **High Customer Switching Costs**: The venture's success assumes customers will replace or augment deeply embedded core HCM systems. This is a major unproven assumption, as high switching costs present a formidable adoption barrier.
- **Temporary AI Advantage**: The "AI-native" differentiation may be short-lived. Incumbents like Workday and SAP are rapidly integrating advanced AI, which could neutralize the venture's primary value proposition and close the window of opportunity.

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **SAM Calculation**: Obtain a detailed, bottom-up calculation for the $12B SAM from the venture team to validate the market size assumption.
- **Formalize Partnership**: Secure a formal, written partnership agreement with ServiceNow to clarify terms, commitments, and risks, moving beyond the current verbal understanding.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Validate Problem-Solution Fit**: Execute Phase 1 of the validation plan by securing formal, written co-design commitments from at least two strategic partners (e.g., Bell Canada, Ateko) within 90 days to confirm enterprise-level interest.
- **Test Willingness to Switch**: Conduct structured interviews with 20-30 target CHROs/CIOs, focusing on current Workday customers, to specifically test the "willingness to replace or augment" assumption, which is the venture's most significant barrier.
- **Confirm Pricing Viability**: Initiate paid MVP pilot programs with 7-10 customers to test the willingness to pay and validate that the ROI supports the proposed premium price point, starting at a $325,000 ACV.
- **Assess Incumbent Threat**: Commission a focused analysis of the AI roadmaps for Workday and SAP SuccessFactors to better quantify the timeline and risk of their AI capabilities neutralizing Novaworks' differentiation.

## Market Size & Segmentation

The Human Capital Management (HCM) market is large and expanding, with a significant, historically underserved segment that Novaworks has targeted for its initial entry. The company's market sizing estimates are generally consistent with third-party research, though its calculation for the serviceable market lacks transparency.

### Market Sizing (TAM, SAM, SOM)

Novaworks operates within the global HCM market, targeting a specific subsegment focused on the deskless workforce. The company's top-down market sizing is outlined below, with confidence levels based on the availability of independent validation.

overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>N/A</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

**Total Addressable Market (TAM**)The global TAM for HCM is estimated at $34.1 billion for 2025 \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 6\], \[DOC: Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx, p. 1\]. This figure is consistent with external market analysis from [Fortune Business Insights](https://www.fortunebusinessinsights.com/industry-reports/human-capital-management-hcm-market-100240), which projects the market will grow from $31.34 billion in 2024 to $64.97 billion by 2032, representing a 9.6% compound annual growth rate (CAGR). A separate forecast from Gartner, focused specifically on HCM software, projects a higher five-year CAGR of 13.6%, with spending expected to exceed $51 billion by 2028 \[DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. unknown\]. The alignment between company claims and independent reports provides high confidence in the overall market size and growth trajectory.

**Serviceable Addressable Market (SAM**)Novaworks defines its SAM as $12 billion, representing the portion of the HCM market focused on its target deskless workforce \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The provided documents do not contain a detailed, bottom-up calculation to substantiate this figure. As this is a single-source company claim without a transparent methodology, confidence in this specific valuation is low. However, the strategic focus on the deskless segment, which comprises approximately 80% of the global workforce, is logical given its scale and historical lack of dedicated technology solutions \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This segment is also identified as a key opportunity in the *Market Dynamics & Growth Drivers* section.

**Serviceable Obtainable Market (SOM**)The company does not state an explicit SOM but implies its target through financial projections. Novaworks aims to capture $77.5 million in annual bookings by 2028 (Year 3) and $199 million by 2030 \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 12\]. This projection represents the company's near-term obtainable market goal. A detailed analysis of the feasibility of these financial targets is outside the scope of this chapter.

### Market Segmentation & Prioritization

Novaworks employs a multi-layered segmentation strategy to define its initial market entry point. The approach prioritizes customer segments based on worker type, company size, technology stack, and industry vertical.

The primary strategic focus is on the deskless workforce, a large segment that traditional HCM systems have not adequately served \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 5\]. To gain initial traction, Novaworks will target a niche within this broad market: mid-sized enterprises that are already invested in the ServiceNow platform \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 11, 14\]. This approach is designed to reduce customer acquisition friction by leveraging a known technology platform and an existing partner ecosystem. The company plans a phased rollout of vertical-specific solutions, beginning with Transportation and Retail, to build expertise and establish proof points before expanding into other industries \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 8\].

## Market Dynamics & Growth Drivers

The Human Capital Management (HCM) market is a large, mature sector undergoing a significant transformation driven by new technology and evolving workforce demands. The market's growth is steady, supported by durable, long-term trends that favor the entry of specialized, AI-native solutions.

### Growth Trajectory and Projections

The global HCM market is substantial and expanding at a consistent rate. Projections for the market's compound annual growth rate (CAGR) range from 8.5% to 9.6% through the next decade \[DOC: Novaworks_TAM_SAM.pptx, p. 1\], [Fortune Business Insights](https://www.fortunebusinessinsights.com/industry-reports/human-capital-management-hcm-market-100240), [Global Growth Insights](https://www.globalgrowthinsights.com/market-reports/human-capital-management-market-101299), [MarketsandMarkets](https://www.marketsandmarkets.com/Market-Reports/human-capital-management-market-193746782.html). Novaworks estimates the market will grow from approximately $34 billion in 2025 to $67 billion by 2032 \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_, p. 6\].

Analysis from Gartner indicates even stronger growth specifically within the HCM software segment, which it projects will exceed $51 billion by 2028 at a five-year CAGR of 13.6% \[DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 2\]. This higher growth rate for software underscores a market shift toward technology-centric solutions over services, driven by large-scale modernization initiatives.

### Key Demand Drivers

Three primary forces are shaping the HCM market's evolution and creating opportunities for new entrants. These drivers are durable and mutually reinforcing, signaling a fundamental shift rather than a temporary trend.

<table class="border-collapse w-full" style="min-width: 75px;">
<colgroup><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"><col style="min-width: 25px;"></colgroup><tbody><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Driver Name</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Description</p></th><th class="border-b-2 border-gray-300 bg-gray-100 font-semibold text-left p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Supporting Evidence</p></th></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>AI and Automation as a Modernization Catalyst</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The integration of Artificial Intelligence is the primary force compelling enterprises to modernize legacy HCM systems. Businesses are investing in AI to increase operational efficiency, reduce costs, and deliver personalized employee experiences at scale.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Gartner identifies multiyear HCM transformation programs as the source of over 50% of forecast spending growth through 2028 [DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 3]. A survey of 349 HR leaders found that AI in HR, skills management, and AI in talent acquisition were their top three most important emerging technologies [DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 9].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Focus on the Underserved Deskless Workforce</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>A significant market opportunity exists in serving the deskless workforce—representing 80% of global employees—which has been historically neglected by traditional HCM technology.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Enterprise leaders are recognizing this gap, with 68% planning to increase investments in technology for this segment, and 44% of deskless workers expecting better tools to simplify their work [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_, p. 6]. Novaworks identifies this as a core inefficiency in the current market [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. 1].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Persistent Need for Compliance and Efficiency</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The ongoing pressure for businesses to "do more with less" and navigate an increasingly complex regulatory landscape creates sustained demand for modern HCM platforms.</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>The need to adhere to labor laws and regulations is a critical driver for adopting robust HCM solutions <a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="underline text-blue-500 hover:text-blue-600 cursor-pointer" href="[https://www.marketresearchfuture.com/reports/human-capital-management-software-market/market-trends">Market](https://www.marketresearchfuture.com/reports/human-capital-management-software-market/market-trends">Market) Research Future</a>. Gartner confirms that a continued focus on compliance and regulations will drive market growth through 2028 [DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 3].</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

### Market Adoption and Timing

The HCM market is at an inflection point. While the core market for HR systems of record is mature, the segment for AI-native platforms is in an early adoption phase. The high prioritization of AI by HR leaders suggests the market is ready for solutions that embed this technology at their core, rather than as an add-on \[DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 9\]. This creates a favorable, "on-time" window for new entrants with an AI-first architecture to challenge incumbents, who are perceived as slower to adapt their legacy platforms \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 29\]. The specific focus on the underserved deskless workforce further sharpens this timing advantage, targeting a large, recognized area of need with limited competition from existing enterprise solutions.

### Potential Headwinds

Despite the positive growth drivers, several factors could temper the market's trajectory or impact a new entrant's success.

- **Incumbent Adaptation**: A central assumption is that large incumbents like Workday and SAP will be slow to integrate AI natively. If these established players accelerate their AI roadmaps and successfully deploy advanced capabilities, the window of opportunity for new, disruptive entrants could close more quickly than anticipated. This threat is further detailed in the *Competitive Landscape & Positioning* section.
- **Economic Uncertainty**: Large-scale HCM transformation projects represent significant capital expenditures. A broad economic downturn could cause enterprises to delay or scale back these initiatives, slowing market growth and extending sales cycles.
- **Pricing and Value Realization**: Gartner notes that HCM software providers are expected to increase subscription prices by an average of 3% to 5% in the coming years \[DOC: Forecast_Analysis_H.pptx, p. 3\]. While this contributes to market revenue growth, it may also increase customer scrutiny on the return on investment, creating pressure for all vendors to clearly demonstrate value.

## Competitive Landscape & Positioning

The Human Capital Management (HCM) market is a mature, multi-billion dollar sector characterized by intense competition among established enterprise suite providers and a dynamic field of specialized mid-market solutions. The primary competitive dynamic is the industry-wide shift toward cloud-based, AI-driven platforms, which is lowering entry barriers for new software firms and forcing incumbents to accelerate innovation \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], [American Edge Project](https://americanedgeproject.org/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/AEP-AI-Paper.pdf). Novaworks enters this environment by positioning itself as an "AI-native" solution built on the ServiceNow platform, targeting the historically underserved deskless workforce \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 2\].

### Direct Competitors

Novaworks faces direct competition from two distinct categories of players: large enterprise suite vendors and agile mid-market specialists. The company's strategy explicitly targets customers of both, aiming to displace mid-market players and execute a "WorkDay take out scenario" within the enterprise segment \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. As noted in the *Market Validation Strategy* section, the feasibility of this "take out" scenario is a critical assumption that requires testing.

### Indirect Competition & Alternative Solutions

The most significant form of competition is the status quo within target organizations. A majority of mid-market and enterprise HR teams operate with fragmented technology stacks, relying on a combination of legacy systems, disparate point solutions for functions like payroll and recruiting, and manual processes \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 22\]. This creates operational inefficiencies and data silos, which Novaworks aims to solve. Additionally, organizations may opt for custom in-house solutions built on platforms like ServiceNow, representing a "build vs. buy" alternative to Novaworks' productized offering.

### Novaworks' Competitive Positioning & Differentiation

Novaworks positions itself to exploit perceived gaps left by both enterprise and mid-market incumbents. Its differentiation strategy is built on four pillars:

1. **Platform-Native Strategy**: By building on ServiceNow, Novaworks aims to leverage a trusted, secure, and extensible enterprise platform. This is intended to reduce customer concerns about partnering with a startup and capitalize on ServiceNow's existing market penetration and "street cred" \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
2. **AI-Native Architecture**: The solution is designed around an agentic AI core, featuring a "voice-enabled SuperAgent," rather than adding AI as a feature to a legacy system. This architecture is claimed as a key defensible moat \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
3. **Target Segment Focus**: The explicit focus on the deskless workforce—a segment representing 80% of global employees—is a core part of the value proposition, addressing a group historically underserved by traditional HCM systems \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
4. **Founder-Market Fit**: The founding team's domain expertise, particularly the CEO's background as a former CHRO, is positioned as a competitive advantage in product design and go-to-market execution \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Competitive Intensity and Potential Threats

The HCM market's competitive intensity is high and expected to increase. The proliferation of open-source AI tools lowers barriers to entry for new software firms, potentially commoditizing parts of the market [American Edge Project](https://americanedgeproject.org/wp-content/uploads/2024/11/AEP-AI-Paper.pdf), [AINVEST](https://www.ainvest.com/news/human-capital-algorithms-encore-search-partners-moat-thrives-ai-driven-world-2507/).

Key threats include:

- **Incumbent AI Adoption**: Enterprise players like SAP and Oracle are actively integrating AI into their platforms, with SAP launching its Joule AI copilot and Oracle introducing AI-driven features [ReportPrime — Top Human Resource Management Market Companies - Rankings, Profiles, SWOT Analysis & Strategic Outlook](https://www.reportprime.com/human-resource-management-r15851/company). This could neutralize Novaworks' "AI-native" advantage over time.
- **New Platform Entrants**: Large technology platforms such as Microsoft and Salesforce are identified as potential future competitors that could enter the HCM space, leveraging their vast enterprise customer bases and technical capabilities \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Platform Dependency**: The venture's reliance on ServiceNow creates a dependency risk. Changes in ServiceNow's strategy, pricing, or platform capabilities could directly impact Novaworks' viability. This is noted as a key issue for analysis in the \[CHAPTER: GTM and Partners\] and is a primary strategic barrier discussed in *Market Entry Barriers & Enablers*.

## Market Entry Barriers & Enablers

The venture's ability to enter the market is defined by a single, powerful enabler—its proposed integration with the ServiceNow ecosystem—which is simultaneously offset by significant customer, regulatory, and strategic barriers. While the ServiceNow partnership provides a potential channel to market, the venture faces high customer switching costs, a complex regulatory landscape for AI in HR, and a fundamental misalignment with Workday's corporate assets.

### Key Barriers and Enablers

<table class="border-collapse w-full" style="min-width: 75px;">

This is the venture's primary enabler for initial market access.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>High Customer Switching Costs</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Barrier</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Core HCM systems are deeply embedded in enterprise operations, creating significant resistance to change.
