# Team and Execution

## Overview

The key team members—CEO Kelley Steven-Waiss, CTO Eswar Vandanapu, and GTM lead Stanimira Koleva—are highly credible, combining prior entrepreneurial exits with deep corporate experience at firms like ServiceNow and Microsoft. This unique blend of skills makes the team exceptionally well-positioned to succeed, particularly in navigating the critical ServiceNow partnership, which is central to their strategy. However, significant talent risks could derail the initiative, including an extreme key-person dependency on the three founders and intense competition for scarce AI talent. The most critical talent gap to fill immediately is the vacant Chief Data & AI Officer role; this position must be filled by an experienced enterprise SaaS leader before the main product build-out begins to validate the company's "AI-native" claims.

### Key Takeaways

- **Exceptional Founder Fit**: The founding team's blend of entrepreneurial success (prior exits) and deep corporate fluency (ex-ServiceNow CEO) is a rare and powerful combination, providing exceptional credibility and navigation skills for the critical ServiceNow partnership.
- **Concentrated Risk Profile**: The venture faces extreme key-person risk, with the three founders covering all critical functions, and a significant capability gap exists with the unfilled Chief Data & AI Officer role, which is vital for an "AI-native" company.

## Risks

- **Founder Over-reliance**: Execution capability is dangerously concentrated in three individuals. The loss of any founder would severely impact the product roadmap and go-to-market strategy, as they currently hold all key leadership roles.
- **Critical Leadership Gap**: The absence of a Chief Data & AI Officer undermines the company's "AI-native" positioning and introduces significant risk to its core product strategy and technical execution.
- **Talent Competition & Retention**: The company must compete for scarce, expensive AI talent against better-funded startups. Failure to attract and retain key engineers could derail the aggressive product timeline.
- **Cultural Friction with Partner**: The team's agile, risk-tolerant startup culture may clash with the processes and priorities of its primary corporate partner, ServiceNow, potentially slowing execution and creating relationship friction.

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **AI Leadership Pipeline**: Request a short-list of candidates and a formal role description for the Chief Data & AI Officer to assess the quality of the talent pipeline and the seriousness of the search.
- **Conflict of Interest Documentation**: Obtain the conflict of interest forms filed by the founders with ServiceNow to understand the specific guardrails and potential limitations on their activities.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Mitigate Founder Over-reliance**: Task the founders with creating a 90-day operational plan that explicitly delegates at least one major responsibility from each founder to a new hire or a senior advisor to test knowledge transfer and reduce bottlenecks.
- **Accelerate AI Leadership Hiring**: Mandate the engagement of a specialized executive search firm within 30 days to fill the Chief Data & AI Officer role, with a target hire date before the January 2026 MVP deadline.
- **Validate Compensation Strategy**: Commission a compensation benchmark analysis within 60 days, specifically against AI-native, venture-backed startups, to ensure the equity and salary packages are competitive enough to attract top talent.
- **Formalize Partner Governance**: Establish a formal monthly check-in between the Novaworks CEO and their primary ServiceNow partnership contact to proactively identify and resolve potential cultural or operational misalignments.

## Core Team Composition & Roles

The founding team comprises three executives with complementary experience in corporate innovation, technology development, and global go-to-market strategy. The initial structure is lean, with the founders covering multiple essential functions. However, the proposed organizational chart for scaling reveals several key roles that are currently unfilled, presenting both an opportunity to attract talent and a near-term execution risk.

### Founding Team and Key Executives

The core team consists of Kelley Steven-Waiss (CEO), Eswar Vandanapu (CTO), and Stanimira Koleva (GTM lead). Their backgrounds combine deep domain expertise in Human Capital Management (HCM), entrepreneurial experience, and experience navigating large technology enterprises like ServiceNow and Microsoft.

She will lead all partnership activities, including the critical relationship with ServiceNow, and build the sales and customer success functions. ### Role Coverage and Identified Gaps

The founding team provides strong initial coverage across the essential roles required for a corporate venture. However, the company's own materials reveal significant gaps between the immediate lean team and the broader organization required to execute its vision. This over-reliance on the founders is a central theme also discussed in the *Talent Risks & Retention Strategy* section.

**Essential Role Coverage:**

- **Innovation Leader & Corporate Navigator:** Kelley Steven-Waiss fills both roles. Her experience as a second-time founder and former Chief Innovation Officer at ServiceNow provides credibility and a vision for the product. Her history within ServiceNow is critical for navigating the partnership central to the company's strategy \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Technical Expert:** Eswar Vandanapu provides the core technical and product development leadership required to build the platform \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Business Developer:** Stanimira Koleva is designated to lead partnerships and GTM, a crucial function given the reliance on the ServiceNow ecosystem. In the interim, Kelley Steven-Waiss will lead founder-led sales \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

**Identified Gaps and Missing Roles:**

- **Chief Data & AI Officer:** The company's investor presentation lists this as a "TBD" role \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 17\]. For a company positioning itself as an "AI-native" solution, the absence of a dedicated leader for data and AI strategy is a critical gap, a point further analyzed in the *Innovation Capability Assessment* and *Talent Sourcing & Development Strategy* sections.
- **Dedicated Product Leadership:** A conflict exists between the company's documents. The due diligence questionnaire states Kelley Steven-Waiss will serve as acting Chief Product Officer, while the investor deck names Melanie Lougee for the role \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 17\]. This suggests that many of the functional heads presented in the pitch deck are aspirational hires rather than committed team members, creating a potential leadership vacuum in key areas like product management, marketing, and design post-funding.
- **Full-Time GTM Leadership:** Stanimira Koleva's planned part-time start, with a transition to full-time in January 2026, leaves a near-term gap in dedicated leadership for the crucial partnership and sales functions during the initial product build-out phase \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

The initial team of 4-5 US-based staff and 10 in India is consistent with the lean structure of modern AI-native startups, which prioritize small, high-agency teams over large headcounts [AI-Native Startup Handbook | Build & Scale Your AI-First Company](https://www.aiatflytbase.com/startup-handbook), [What every startup can learn from AI-native hiring: Smaller teams, higher salaries, and the ‘Super IC’](https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring). However, the heavy reliance on the three founders to cover numerous strategic functions simultaneously creates significant key-person risk.

## Innovation Capability Assessment

The Novaworks team demonstrates a rare and valuable combination of proven entrepreneurial execution and deep corporate fluency. The founders have direct experience building and successfully exiting technology startups, complemented by extensive careers navigating the complex internal environments of large enterprises they now target as customers. This blend of capabilities is critical for executing an ambitious product vision that depends on both rapid innovation and a strategic partnership with a major platform provider.

### Entrepreneurial and Technical Competence

The core leadership team possesses a credible track record of building technology companies from inception. CEO Kelley Steven-Waiss is a second-time founder, having previously founded Hitch Works, a talent mobility platform acquired by ServiceNow [Justia Patents](https://patents.justia.com/inventor/steven-kelley), \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This prior success provides direct evidence of her ability to build a product, achieve market traction, and navigate a successful exit. Similarly, CTO Eswar Vandanapu is a serial entrepreneur and a "successful exited CTO" who has also built and sold an operations business in India \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

The team's technical competence is centered on Vandanapu, whose background includes engineering leadership at Oracle and serving as CTO for a 350-person Series C company \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The planned organizational structure includes identified leaders for key technical roles such as ServiceNow architecture, mobile development, and data engineering \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 17\]. However, two notable challenges exist. First, the company is pre-product due to intellectual property constraints, meaning the team has not yet executed on this specific vision together \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. Second, the Chief Data & AI Officer role remains unfilled, a significant gap for a company positioning itself as an "AI-native" solution, as also noted in Core Team Composition & Roles \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 17\].

### Corporate Fluency and Network Strength

The team is exceptionally well-equipped to navigate the corporate landscape. Steven-Waiss's experience as a former CHRO and Chief Innovation Officer provides her with the perspective of a target buyer, deep domain expertise, and a "network of other buyers that trust her" \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This insider knowledge is critical for product-market fit and sales execution. Stanimira Koleva, Head of Global GTM, brings extensive experience managing large-scale partnerships at companies like Cisco, Citrix, and Microsoft, which is directly applicable to managing the crucial ServiceNow relationship \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

This corporate fluency is amplified by a formidable network. The company has assembled two advisory boards: one with senior executives from ServiceNow, PeopleSoft, and Aon, and another composed entirely of CHROs from major enterprises including Cigna, Petco, and Bell Canada \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 18\]. This network, detailed further in *Talent Sourcing & Development Strategy*, provides unparalleled access to market feedback, potential design partners, and strategic guidance. The team has already leveraged these connections to establish "customer zero" relationships with ServiceNow and Bell Canada, demonstrating an ability to translate network access into tangible business opportunities \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Learning Velocity and Iteration

Novaworks has outlined an aggressive development timeline that prioritizes rapid learning and iteration. The plan is to deliver a limited MVP by January for partner feedback, followed by a full MVP release in May to coincide with the ServiceNow Knowledge event \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The product development process is structured in three phases: building foundational capabilities based on the core vision, refining requirements with design partners, and rapidly iterating based on early sales objections \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This approach indicates a strong orientation toward hypothesis-driven development and market validation. While this planned velocity is high, it remains untested, as the team has not yet begun development post-funding.

### Capability Summary

The following table assesses the team's innovation capabilities.

executives and target CHRO customers, which has already yielded commitments for "customer zero" pilots [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 18].</p></td></tr></tbody>

## Talent Sourcing & Development Strategy

Novaworks' talent strategy prioritizes capital efficiency and deep product expertise in its initial phase, followed by a rapid scaling of go-to-market (GTM) and customer-facing roles post-launch. The approach relies on a lean, geographically distributed team, augmented by strategic contractors and a robust advisory network to fill immediate expertise gaps. However, a critical leadership role in AI remains unfilled, and a formal plan for team development is not yet defined.

### External Hiring Strategy

The company plans a phased hiring approach, beginning with a lean R&D-focused team and expanding significantly after the product's minimum viable product (MVP) is established. This aligns with hiring patterns of other AI-native startups that concentrate headcount in engineering and data teams while remaining lean in commercial functions [Ravio](https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring), [AI at FlytBase](https://www.aiatflytbase.com/startup-handbook).

The initial team at launch will consist of approximately 15 people: 4-5 employees in the US, 1 in Dubai, and 10 in India \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This core group is projected to expand to 47 full-time employees within the first 15 months, with R&D roles comprising 56% of the initial year's personnel expense \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 15, 16\].

A key vulnerability in the hiring plan is the vacant Chief Data & AI Officer position, a critical role for an AI-native company, as highlighted in both the *Core Team Composition & Roles* and *Innovation Capability Assessment* sections \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 17\]. Filling this role is the most immediate priority to ensure the product's technical and strategic direction aligns with its core value proposition. The plan to hire more AI specialists is contingent on available capital, which could delay roadmap acceleration \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

The hiring plan prioritizes roles as outlined below:

<table class="border-collapse w-full" style="min-width: 125px;">

Product Team</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>India / US</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Q1 2026</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>To build and launch the MVP, focusing on R&amp;D as the primary initial function [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Post-Launch Scaling (Year 1)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Head of Product Marketing, Head of Customer Experience, Head of Product Design, Head of Operations &amp; Finance</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>US</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>H2 2026</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>To build out the GTM, customer success, and operational functions required to support initial sales and market launch [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 17].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p><strong>Growth Phase (Year 2)</strong></p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Direct Sales &amp; Customer Success</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>US / Global</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>2027</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>To scale the sales engine beyond founder-led efforts as market demand dictates [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

### Advisory Network

Novaworks has established a strong advisory network that serves as a primary source of strategic guidance and industry access, compensating for the lean initial team. The network is structured into two distinct groups:

- **CEO Advisors**: This group includes senior executives with deep operational and technical experience, including several current and former ServiceNow leaders (Pat Casey, Manish Shah, Rag Bhagavatha). This provides Novaworks with critical domain expertise and an informal channel to navigate its strategic partnership with ServiceNow \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 18\].
- **Industry CHRO Advisory Board**: Comprising Chief Human Resources Officers from target customers like Bell Canada, ServiceNow, and Cigna, this board offers direct access to the target buyer persona. This group is positioned to provide invaluable feedback for product development and validation, and potentially serve as a source for early customer introductions \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 18\].

Additionally, former founding team member Manish Shah will act as an advisor, leveraging his healthcare industry network for future vertical expansion \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Partner Resources

To accelerate development while managing costs, Novaworks plans to augment its core engineering team with contractors sourced from strategic partners and investors \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This strategy provides flexibility to meet the aggressive MVP timeline for the ServiceNow partner kickoff in January and the full launch in May. While this approach allows for rapid scaling, it also introduces dependencies on third-party resources for critical path development. The implications of this on intellectual property are addressed in the \[CHAPTER: Legal and IP\].

### Team Development Plan

The provided documents do not contain a formal strategy for employee training or skill development. At this pre-launch stage, development is expected to be informal, driven by the hands-on process of building the product and engaging with design partners. The advisory boards are a significant asset for mentoring the executive team. Furthermore, CEO Kelley Steven-Waiss has established a core principle that "everyone is in Sales," requiring all leaders to be customer-facing \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This mandate serves as an informal mechanism for cross-functional development, ensuring that technical and product teams maintain a direct connection to market needs.

## Team Structure & Governance

Novaworks plans to operate with a lean, founder-led organizational model designed for capital efficiency and rapid execution, a structure consistent with benchmarks for AI-native startups \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], [AI at FlytBase](https://www.aiatflytbase.com/startup-handbook). The governance framework relies on a combination of a formal board, strategic partner integration, and an industry-focused advisory council to guide strategy and maintain accountability.

### Reporting Structure and Organizational Design

The initial organizational structure is flat, concentrating on product development while outsourcing general and administrative functions \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. At launch, the team will consist of 15-17 people distributed across the US (4-5), Dubai (1), and India (10) \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This R&D-heavy allocation aligns with the company's Year 1 budget, which dedicates 56% of FTE expense to R&D, and is typical for AI-native companies that prioritize engineering and data talent over commercial functions in the early stages \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 15\], [Ravio](https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring).

The proposed Board of Directors will provide formal oversight, with a structure designed to integrate key stakeholders.

| Proposed Board Role | Description | \*\*| :--- | :--- | \**| **Executive Directors*** *| The CEO (Kelley Steven-Waiss) and CTO (Eswar Vandanapu) will hold board seats, ensuring direct operational linkage.* \*| \**| **Investor Director*** *| The lead investor will have a dedicated seat, providing financial oversight and strategic guidance.* \*| \**| **Partner Directors*** *| Representation from key partners Ateko and Bell Canada is planned, intended to align product and go-to-market strategies with crucial early customers and channels.* \*| \**| **Independent Director*** *| One independent director with SaaS and early-stage growth experience will be mutually selected to provide impartial expertise and governance.* \*| ***Source: \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]***

This board composition provides a direct line of accountability to investors and strategic partners. The board is expected to meet quarterly and on an as-needed basis \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Decision Rights

Decision-making authority is concentrated within the founding team to facilitate speed. Responsibilities are clearly delineated:

- **Kelley Steven-Waiss (CEO)**: Leads overall strategy, product vision, sales, and operations, acting as the central decision-maker for commercial and product direction \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Eswar Vandanapu (CTO)**: Holds authority over technology execution, technical strategy, inbound product management, and leadership of the India-based development team \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **Stanimira Koleva (GTM Lead)**: Manages partnerships, global go-to-market efforts, and sales operations \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

This structure minimizes bureaucracy but places significant operational load on the three key executives, creating a potential bottleneck risk as the company scales.

### Integration Points

The governance model incorporates several formal integration points to connect the team with key partners and the target market:

- **Board-Level Integration**: The inclusion of Ateko and Bell Canada on the proposed board creates a formal channel for strategic alignment with launch customers and go-to-market partners \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].
- **CHRO Advisory Board**: The company plans to establish an advisory board of Chief Human Resources Officers and other industry experts. This group will serve as a direct feedback channel from the target buyer persona, influencing product requirements and market positioning \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\], \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 18\].
- **Partner Operations**: The go-to-market strategy relies on co-sell and co-market motions with ServiceNow, requiring deep operational integration with ServiceNow's sales and partnership teams \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Performance Metrics & Communication

As a pre-product company, initial performance metrics are milestone-based rather than financial. The primary goals are product delivery and early market validation:

1. Deliver a minimum viable product (MVP) for the ServiceNow partner kickoff in January 2026.
2. Release a full MVP and exit stealth mode for the ServiceNow Knowledge event in May 2026.
3. Secure 7-10 design partners or prospective customers by the end of June 2026. \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]

The team has established a clear communication cadence to ensure accountability. Management plans to review progress, cash burn, and other key performance indicators on a monthly basis. A monthly newsletter will be distributed to investors and advisors to report on progress against these milestones \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

## Team Dynamics & Culture

The Novaworks team exhibits a culture and dynamic well-suited for an early-stage venture, characterized by a hands-on leadership style, a lean operational ethos, and a high tolerance for risk. However, this startup culture must navigate the complexities of its deep integration with and dependence on a large corporate partner, ServiceNow, which presents a significant potential for friction.

### Leadership Style and Vision

The leadership approach is founder-led, customer-centric, and intensely hands-on. CEO Kelley Steven-Waiss articulates a core principle that "everyone is in Sales," indicating an expectation for all team members to be customer-facing and commercially aware \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This directive style is balanced by a desire for collaborative partnership, seeking investors who will "brainstorm with us" \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The company's stated core values—including "Be Bold," "Learn Fast," and "Win Together"—reinforce a vision for a culture centered on innovation, agility, and collaboration \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Team Chemistry and Work Style

The team has established a lean, agile work style focused on capital efficiency and rapid iteration. A key decision was to forgo hiring a founding COO to "keep organization lean" and manage cash burn, instead retaining the individual as an advisor \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This pragmatic decision suggests the team can align on difficult strategic choices. The operational plan prioritizes R&D and product development, with a phased approach to validate requirements with design partners before a full launch \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This model aligns with established benchmarks for AI-native startups, which emphasize small, cross-functional teams and high-agency operators over early headcount growth [AI at FlytBase](https://www.aiatflytbase.com/startup-handbook), [Ravio](https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring). The plan for developers to handle initial customer support further reinforces a culture of ownership and tight customer feedback loops \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\].

### Risk Tolerance and Resilience

The founding team demonstrates a high tolerance for ambiguity and risk, which is necessary for its ambitious goal of disrupting the established HCM market. Both the CEO and CTO are described as second-time or serial entrepreneurs, indicating comfort with the startup lifecycle \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. They explicitly acknowledge the risks of competing with incumbents like Workday and SAP but believe that "AI lowered the barriers to entry to take out the Giants" \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. This perspective shows an awareness of competitive threats combined with a conviction in their strategic timing and approach.

### Cultural Alignment and Potential Friction

Novaworks' culture is fundamentally shaped by its symbiotic relationship with ServiceNow, which is both an asset and a source of potential conflict. The founders' status as current ServiceNow employees provides them with invaluable insider knowledge to navigate the partnership. However, this dual identity creates a significant challenge in balancing the fast-paced, risk-tolerant culture of a startup with the processes and politics of a large public company. While the team has filed conflict of interest forms, the risk of encountering "corporate antibodies" remains \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown\]. The primary cultural friction point will be maintaining agility and entrepreneurial speed while adhering to the governance and strategic priorities of its primary partner and distribution channel.

## Talent Risks & Retention Strategy

The primary talent risks for Novaworks center on its significant reliance on the founding team and the intense competition for specialized AI talent. While the team's experience is a core asset, its lean structure creates operational vulnerabilities. Mitigation strategies must focus on distributing knowledge, offering competitive compensation, and deliberately building a resilient organizational culture to manage the pressures of rapid growth.

### Key Person Risk

Novaworks exhibits a high degree of key person risk, with critical strategic and operational functions concentrated within its three founders. Kelley Steven-Waiss (CEO) is also acting as the Chief Product Officer, Chief Sales Officer, and COO \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. 6\]. Eswar Vandanapu (CTO) leads all technology, product management, India operations, and technical customer success, while Stanimira Koleva is responsible for all global go-to-market and partnership activities \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 6\]. The departure of any founder, particularly in the first 18-24 months, would severely disrupt product development and market entry.

While an investor deck names a Chief Product Officer, the more recent due diligence questionnaire clarifies that the CEO currently holds this role, indicating a fluid, founder-centric leadership structure \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 17\], \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. 6\]. The company's plan to hire a Chief Data & AI Officer is a necessary step to begin distributing this concentrated responsibility \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 17\].

### Retention Risk and Mitigation

The company faces substantial retention risk driven by the competitive market for AI talent. AI-native startups operate with smaller teams and pay a 36% median salary premium compared to other startups, placing significant pressure on Novaworks' compensation strategy [Ravio](https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring). The company's plan to maintain a lean headcount of 53 employees through Year 3 while ARR is projected to grow 134% implies high individual workloads, increasing the risk of attrition \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf, p. 16\].

To mitigate these risks, Novaworks has established a standard equity incentive structure with a 10% option pool reserved post-funding and four-year vesting with a one-year cliff \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 15, 16\]. However, cash and equity compensation must be benchmarked directly against other AI-native firms to remain competitive. Non-financial incentives, such as the compelling mission to serve the deskless workforce and the founders' strong industry reputations, will be critical for attracting and retaining key personnel.

### Succession and Scaling Risk

At this pre-seed stage, Novaworks has no formal succession plan, creating a vulnerability should a key leader depart unexpectedly. The pre-funding departure of a founding team member, Manish Shah, highlights the potential for early-stage team volatility, even though he remains an advisor \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. 7\]. The company's extensive advisory board provides strategic depth but cannot substitute for executive leadership in daily operations \[DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29*.pdf, p. 18\]. As the company scales, a deliberate strategy for identifying and developing internal talent for leadership roles will be necessary to build organizational resilience.

### Culture and Burnout Risk

The combination of an aggressive roadmap, a lean staffing model, and the founders' plan to defer salaries until January 2026 creates a significant risk of team burnout \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-*Novaworks.pdf, p. 7, 13\]. The "everyone is in Sales" mentality, while fostering an all-hands-on-deck approach, can blur roles and increase pressure if not managed carefully \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-*Novaworks.pdf, p. 26\]. A long-term integration risk also exists; the high-agency, capital-efficient culture that is effective at the startup stage may face challenges integrating into a larger corporate structure following a potential acquisition, which is noted as a possible exit path \[DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW*-\_Novaworks.pdf, p. 7\].

The table below summarizes the primary talent-related risks and corresponding mitigation strategies.

compete for scarce AI talent against startups paying a 36% salary premium, while its lean staffing model increases pressure on each team member, elevating flight risk <a target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer" class="underline text-blue-500 hover:text-blue-600 cursor-pointer" href="[https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring">Ravio</a>,](https://ravio.com/blog/ai-native-startup-hiring">Ravio,) [DOC: Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf, p. 16].</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Benchmark compensation and equity packages specifically against AI-native startups and emphasize the compelling mission and direct impact employees will have in a small team to supplement financial incentives [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. 16].</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Team Burnout</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Aggressive product deadlines, a lean staffing model, and founders initially deferring salaries create conditions for potential team burnout, which could jeopardize roadmap execution [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. 7, 13].</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Implement formal project management to monitor workloads, clearly define scope for the Minimum Viable Product (MVP) to avoid overwork, and establish a culture that encourages open communication about capacity.</p></td></tr><tr class="border-b border-gray-200"><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Lack of Formal Succession</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>No formal succession plan exists for key leadership roles, meaning the departure of a founder would significantly disrupt operations and product development [DOC: Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf, p. unknown].</p></td><td class="border border-gray-200 p-2 break-words overflow-wrap-anywhere min-w-0" colspan="1" rowspan="1"><p>Identify and mentor high-potential individuals within the initial team for future leadership roles and cross-train team members on critical systems and processes to build redundancy.</p></td></tr></tbody>
</table>

## Claims

 1. The founding team consists of Kelley Steven-Waiss (CEO), Eswar Vandanapu (CTO), and Stanimira Koleva (GTM lead).
 2. CEO Kelley Steven-Waiss is a former Chief Innovation Officer at ServiceNow and founder of Hitch Works, which was acquired by ServiceNow.
 3. The Chief Data & AI Officer role is currently unfilled.
 4. The initial team will consist of 15-17 people, with 10 located in India.
 5. The company has two advisory boards: one with senior technology executives and one with CHROs from target customers.
 6. Stanimira Koleva, the Head of Global GTM, will join full-time in January 2026.
 7. The company plans to deliver a limited MVP by January 2026 and a full MVP by May 2026.
 8. R&D roles are projected to comprise 56% of the first year's personnel expense.
 9. A 10% option pool is reserved for employee incentives post-funding.
10. The proposed Board of Directors includes representation from partners Ateko and Bell Canada.

# Legal and IP

## Overview

Novaworks' legal and intellectual property landscape is defined by its pre-product stage and deep integration with ServiceNow. The venture has a clear plan to develop proprietary IP around its AI-native HCM platform, particularly its "Nova AI Architecture" and "Nova HR Codex." However, significant risks exist. A critical dependency is an unformalized "verbal agreement" to license ServiceNow IP, which includes a grant-back clause that could encumber future developments. Furthermore, the platform's core function—processing sensitive employee data with AI—places it in a high-risk category under emerging regulations like the EU AI Act, creating a substantial future compliance burden that has not yet been fully addressed.

### Key Takeaways

- **Critical Fact 1**: A verbal, non-exclusive license for ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" IP includes a grant-back clause, creating a significant unmitigated risk that could encumber the value and exclusivity of Novaworks' own future intellectual property.
- **Critical Fact 2**: The venture's core business in AI-driven Human Capital Management is classified as "high-risk" under emerging global regulations like the EU AI Act, which will impose stringent compliance obligations and significant operational costs.

## Risks

- **IP Encumbrance**: The informal verbal agreement to license ServiceNow IP, which includes a grant-back clause, poses a material risk of limiting the defensibility and commercial value of Novaworks' proprietary technology \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\].
- **Regulatory Compliance Burden**: As an AI platform for employment, the solution falls into a "high-risk" category under the EU AI Act and faces a complex patchwork of global data privacy laws, creating a significant and costly compliance burden that is not yet fully planned for [Cimplifi](https://www.cimplifi.com/resources/the-updated-state-of-ai-regulations-for-2025/?utm_source=openai).
- **Unsecured IP Ownership**: The company has not yet executed IP assignment agreements with its founders or employees, creating a foundational risk to the ownership and clean title of any intellectual property developed post-funding \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\].
- **Data Handling Liability**: The platform will process sensitive employee data without a defined data governance, security, or privacy strategy, exposing the venture to significant legal and reputational liability under regulations like GDPR and CCPA [Capstone](https://capstonedc.com/insights/growing-regulatory-risks-for-ai-driven-human-capital-management-platforms/).

## Next Steps

**Additional Evidence**

- **ServiceNow Agreement Draft**: Obtain a draft of the proposed written IP license agreement with ServiceNow to allow for a formal legal review of its terms, particularly the scope of the grant-back provision.

**Derisking Actions**

- **Formalize IP License**: Engage legal counsel to negotiate and formalize the ServiceNow IP license into a written agreement that clearly defines usage rights and minimizes the impact of the grant-back clause.
- **Execute IP Assignments**: Immediately upon funding, draft and execute comprehensive IP assignment agreements with all founders, employees, and contractors to secure ownership of all developed IP.
- **Develop Compliance Roadmap**: Engage specialized legal counsel to create a preliminary roadmap for compliance with key regulations, specifically the EU AI Act and relevant US/EU data privacy laws.
- **Establish Data Governance Policy**: Develop a foundational data governance and privacy policy that outlines the protocols for collecting, storing, and processing sensitive employee data in alignment with major regulatory frameworks.

## Potential Intellectual Property (IP) Considerations

Based on the Novaworks proposal and supporting documents, the company's intellectual property (IP) strategy is centered on developing proprietary AI-native technology while carefully managing potential IP contamination from the founders' current employment.

### Potential for New IP Creation

Novaworks is a pre-product company and has intentionally avoided creating IP to prevent "tainted IP" issues stemming from the founders' association with ServiceNow \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. However, the company has identified several areas where it plans to create defensible IP post-funding. The core of this new IP appears to be in the application of AI to the Human Capital Management (HCM) domain, specifically through its planned AI architecture and proprietary data assets \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=I6mRBPZs85V8JO234MA62nCqiNfjKRkoP1EVIdd%2Fcek%3D), p. unknown\].

Key areas identified for potential IP creation include:

- **Proprietary AI Architecture:** The proposed "Nova AI Architecture" includes several custom-named components such as the "Nova Agent Layer," "Nova SLM" (Small Language Model), "Nova Transformers," and a "Nova Vector DB." The unique integration and orchestration of these elements could be protected as a trade secret \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=I6mRBPZs85V8JO234MA62nCqiNfjKRkoP1EVIdd%2Fcek%3D), p. unknown\].
- **Nova HR Codex:** The company plans to build a "Nova HR Codex for Global Compliance," which appears to be a proprietary knowledge base designed to provide automated compliance capabilities \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. This curated dataset and its application represent a significant potential IP asset. This codex is also central to the venture's compliance strategy, as discussed in the *Potential Future Regulatory or Compliance Considerations* section.
- **Agentic Workflows:** The solution's value proposition is based on "agentic and conversational experiences" that create a "personal assistant" for each employee \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. The specific business methods and processes embedded in these agentic workflows could constitute protectable IP.

### Leveraging Third-Party IP

Novaworks states it is not currently using any externally owned IP \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. However, the company discloses a significant dependency on ServiceNow's technology. Specifically, Novaworks has a "verbal agreement to utilize the Skills Intelligence of ServiceNow through a non-exclusive license" \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. This arrangement includes a critical grant-back clause that "requires sharing of any modifications made to that IP back to ServiceNow," which could encumber future IP development and limit its exclusive value \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. The company also plans to build its AI capabilities using publicly available LLMs and open-source toolkits like Langchain, meaning its IP will lie in the application rather than foundational models \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\].

### Stated IP Protection Considerations

The company's primary stated consideration is the avoidance of creating IP before the founders fully separate from ServiceNow \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\]. The provided materials do not detail a formal strategy for protecting future IP (e.g., patent filings vs. trade secret policy).

A key administrative gap exists regarding IP ownership. The company confirms that employees have not yet executed IP assignment agreements, stating this will be done "when our formal employment starts" post-funding \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. unknown\].

### Preliminary Assessment of Potential IP

Novaworks' potential to create valuable IP is centered on its specialized AI applications, proprietary datasets like the "Nova HR Codex," and unique workflow architecture built upon the ServiceNow platform. The founders' awareness of "IP taint" is a positive signal of legal sophistication.

However, two areas warrant significant attention during formal diligence:

1. **ServiceNow IP Agreement:** The verbal, non-exclusive license for ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" must be formalized in a written agreement. The scope of the grant-back provision needs to be clearly defined by legal counsel to assess its potential impact on the long-term value and defensibility of Novaworks' own IP.
2. **IP Assignment:** Ensuring all founders, employees, and contractors execute comprehensive IP assignment agreements immediately upon funding is critical to establish a clean chain of title for all newly developed intellectual property.

If the venture progresses, a formal review by IP counsel is essential to formalize the ServiceNow relationship, secure ownership of all created IP, and develop a clear protection strategy.

## Data Usage, Privacy & Third-Party Dependency Considerations

Based on the Novaworks proposal and supporting documents, the venture's operating model presents several considerations regarding data handling and external dependencies that require further diligence.

### Data Usage Profile

The venture's core product is an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform designed to manage the entire employee lifecycle, from hiring to retirement \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. 11\], \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=I6mRBPZs85V8JO234MA62nCqiNfjKRkoP1EVIdd%2Fcek%3D), p. 7\]. This function inherently involves the collection, processing, and storage of sensitive employee personal data and confidential corporate information, such as performance metrics, compensation, and organizational structure. The company's AI architecture diagram also indicates plans to use "Public Data" and "Partner Data" within its data lakehouse, though the specific nature, sourcing, and usage rights for this external data are not detailed \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=I6mRBPZs85V8JO234MA62nCqiNfjKRkoP1EVIdd%2Fcek%3D), p. 10\].

The provided materials do not specify the measures for handling this sensitive data, nor do they outline security protocols or a strategy for compliance with data privacy regulations. Given that AI-driven HCM platforms face increasing regulatory scrutiny over their handling of employee data, this is a notable gap [Capstone](https://capstonedc.com/insights/growing-regulatory-risks-for-ai-driven-human-capital-management-platforms/). Compliance with frameworks such as the California Consumer Privacy Act (CCPA) and the EU's General Data Protection Regulation (GDPR) will be critical for market access and risk mitigation [TrustArc](https://trustarc.com/resource/us-consumer-privacy-laws-2025-update/). A more detailed analysis of the evolving regulatory landscape is available in the *Potential Future Regulatory or Compliance Considerations* section.

### Third-Party Dependencies

Novaworks' technical and operational strategy relies heavily on a multi-layered stack of third-party technologies and data.

### Stated Considerations & Consultations

The proposal materials do not explicitly discuss data privacy impact assessments, specific security protocols, or a compliance roadmap for relevant regulations. Furthermore, there is no mention of plans for consultation with internal or external IT Security, Data Governance, or Legal counsel regarding data handling, privacy policies, or the terms of use for third-party software and AI models.

### Preliminary Assessment of Data & Third-Party Considerations

The venture's reliance on sensitive employee data and a complex web of third-party technologies introduces material risks that require formal legal and technical review. The absence of a defined data privacy and security strategy is a critical omission that must be addressed before product development progresses.

Key areas for further diligence include:

- **Third-Party Licenses:** The use of open-source components like Langchain and commercial LLMs necessitates a thorough review of all associated licenses by legal counsel to ensure compatibility with Novaworks' commercial model and to prevent IP contamination or restrictive usage terms [FutureSkillGuides](https://www.futureskillguides.com/ai-regulation-compliance-global-overview-2025/).
- **IP Agreement Formalization:** The "verbal agreement" with ServiceNow for its Skills Intelligence IP must be formalized into a written contract that clearly defines licensing terms, usage rights, and the scope of the share-back provision.
- **Data Governance:** A comprehensive data governance and privacy policy must be developed to address the handling of employee PII and comply with regulations in target markets. This should include conducting a Privacy Impact Assessment (PIA) to mitigate risks associated with processing personal data [TrustArc](https://trustarc.com/resource/us-consumer-privacy-laws-2025-update/).

Early consultation with legal, IT security, and data governance specialists is essential to establish a sound foundation for the company's operations and mitigate potential liabilities.

## Potential Future Regulatory or Compliance Considerations

Based on the Novaworks proposal and its described concept, the venture operates in a domain with significant and evolving regulatory oversight.

### Potential for Future Regulated Application

The venture is an AI-native Human Capital Management (HCM) platform, a sector inherently governed by employment laws and data privacy regulations \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. 1\]. The company's stated market is "Global," which subjects it to international regulatory frameworks \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. 26\]. Furthermore, Novaworks explicitly plans to target highly regulated industries; its capability roadmap includes phased entry into sectors such as healthcare, transportation, and manufacturing \[DOC: [Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29\_.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Novaworks_Presentation_Deck_Colle_Capital_082225.final_29_.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=I6mRBPZs85V8JO234MA62nCqiNfjKRkoP1EVIdd%2Fcek%3D), p. 8\]. The company also notes that a former team member's experience in healthcare will be valuable when it begins to "attack regulated segments" \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. 7\].

### Anticipated Future Regulatory/Compliance Landscape

As an AI-driven platform operating globally in the HCM space, Novaworks will need to navigate a complex, multi-jurisdictional legal landscape. Key future considerations include:

- **Artificial Intelligence Regulation:** The European Union's AI Act, with enforcement beginning in 2026, establishes a risk-based framework for AI systems [Cimplifi](https://www.cimplifi.com/resources/the-updated-state-of-ai-regulations-for-2025/?utm_source=openai). AI used in employment and workforce management, including recruiting, is classified as "high-risk" and subject to strict requirements for risk management, data governance, transparency, and human oversight [Cimplifi](https://www.cimplifi.com/resources/the-updated-state-of-ai-regulations-for-2025/?utm_source=openai). Non-compliance can result in fines of up to 7% of global annual turnover, making this a critical consideration for Novaworks' planned global operations [FutureSkillGuides](https://www.futureskillguides.com/ai-regulation-compliance-global-overview-2025/). In the U.S., there is a growing patchwork of state-level AI laws, and federal agencies like the FTC are applying existing consumer protection laws to address algorithmic bias in hiring and employment [Capstone](https://capstonedc.com/insights/growing-regulatory-risks-for-ai-driven-human-capital-management-platforms/).
- **Data Privacy Laws:** The company will process sensitive employee data, making it subject to numerous data privacy laws. In the U.S., this includes a growing list of state-level regulations such as the California Consumer Privacy Act (CCPA) [Capstone](https://capstonedc.com/insights/growing-regulatory-risks-for-ai-driven-human-capital-management-platforms/). As of 2025, at least 17 states have enacted such laws, creating a complex compliance environment [trustarc.com](https://trustarc.com/resource/us-consumer-privacy-laws-2025-update/). Global operations would also bring regulations like the GDPR into scope.
- **Industry-Specific Compliance:** Entry into planned vertical markets like healthcare will introduce stringent, industry-specific requirements, such as HIPAA in the United States, which governs the use and protection of health information.

### Stated Awareness & Future Planning

Novaworks demonstrates an awareness of the importance of compliance, listing "automated compliance" as a key product differentiator and planning to build a "Nova HR Codex for Global Compliance" to create a competitive moat \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. 31\]. This codex was also identified as a key potential IP asset in the *Potential Intellectual Property (IP) Considerations* section. However, the provided materials do not specify which regulations this codex will address or detail the strategy for keeping it current with rapidly evolving laws like the EU AI Act.

### Proposed Future Consultation

The venture's documentation does not explicitly mention plans for future consultation with specialized legal or compliance counsel regarding emerging AI and data privacy regulations. The company notes it uses Cooley LLC for general corporate matters but is considering a new firm post-funding \[DOC: [Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW\_-\_Novaworks.pdf](https://zapistorageprod.blob.core.windows.net/organization-project-documents/organization-39/project-2632/Stalwart_Ventures_Diligence_Questionnaire_KSW_-_Novaworks.pdf?sv=2025-07-05&st=2025-11-17T19%3A39%3A29Z&se=2027-11-18T07%3A39%3A29Z&sr=b&sp=r&sig=FXgdizRjAxH2mHNChkp9Q5JAze2o50kHBHWaRiT9My0%3D), p. 11\].

### Preliminary Assessment of Future Regulatory Needs

While Novaworks' plan to embed compliance into its product is a positive indicator, its success is contingent on navigating a highly complex and dynamic global regulatory environment. The classification of AI in HR as "high-risk" under the EU AI Act presents a significant future compliance hurdle that will require substantial investment in governance, transparency, and risk management. The lack of a detailed strategy to address specific emerging AI and data privacy laws is a notable gap. Proactive engagement with specialized regulatory counsel will be critical to de-risk the product development roadmap and ensure the "Nova HR Codex" is a defensible asset rather than a potential liability.

## Overall Preliminary Legal/IP Assessment & Key Future Considerations

**Preliminary Assessment of Potential Considerations (Based on Venture Proposal):**

Based on the Novaworks proposal, the concept appears to present opportunities for novel IP creation within AI-driven Human Capital Management and involves the use of sensitive employee data, which will require careful handling. The venture's reliance on third-party IP from ServiceNow under a verbal agreement and its operation in a domain classified as "high-risk" by emerging AI regulations are the most significant immediate considerations.

This assessment is preliminary and based solely on the provided concept information.

**Key Future Legal/IP Consultation Points (If Venture Proceeds):**

If Novaworks progresses beyond this initial concept stage, proactive consultation with relevant internal corporate teams would be advisable on the following:

**Intellectual Property:**

- Formal review by the Corporate IP Team to assess any novel algorithms, software, or processes developed for potential patentability or trade secret protection.

- Guidance on proper documentation and procedures for capturing any new IP generated by the venture team.

- Immediate legal review and formalization of the ServiceNow "Skills Intelligence" license to clarify terms and mitigate risks from the grant-back clause.

**Data Handling & Privacy:**

- Review by the Data Governance Office and/or Legal (Privacy) regarding the proposed collection, storage, and use of employee personal data, ensuring alignment with corporate policies and applicable regulations like GDPR and CCPA.

- Consultation with IT Security on appropriate safeguards for any data processed or stored by the venture's solution.

**Third-Party Components & Agreements:**

- Review by Legal/IP Team of any third-party software licenses (especially open-source components with copyleft provisions like Langchain) or API terms of use to ensure compliance and avoid unintended IP encumbrances.

**Regulatory & Compliance (Future Scope):**

- If the venture explores externalization or expands into heavily regulated internal areas, consultation with Corporate Legal and/or Compliance will be necessary to understand and plan for applicable regulatory requirements, particularly the EU AI Act.

**General:**

- Execution of IP assignment agreements for all founders and employees to ensure a clean chain of title for all created IP.
- Periodic check-ins with the Legal Department as the venture evolves to address any emerging legal or contractual considerations.

**Conclusion & Recommendation for Internal Consultation:**

The Novaworks concept presents several areas where proactive legal and IP guidance will be beneficial if development proceeds. Early and ongoing engagement with the corporation's internal Legal, IP, Data Governance, and Compliance teams, as appropriate for each stage of development, is strongly recommended to ensure the venture aligns with corporate policies, protects corporate assets, and mitigates potential risks.

## Claims

 1. Novaworks has intentionally avoided creating intellectual property to prevent "tainted IP" issues related to the founders' current employment.
 2. The company plans to create proprietary IP centered on its "Nova AI Architecture" and a "Nova HR Codex for Global Compliance."
 3. Novaworks has a verbal agreement to use ServiceNow's "Skills Intelligence" through a non-exclusive license.
 4. The verbal license agreement with ServiceNow includes a grant-back clause requiring Novaworks to share any modifications to the licensed IP.
 5. Novaworks employees have not yet executed intellectual property assignment agreements.
 6. The venture's platform will collect, process, and store sensitive employee personal data as part of its core function.
 7. The company's AI architecture will be built using publicly available and commercial LLMs, as well as open-source toolkits like Langchain.
 8. Novaworks plans to target highly regulated industries, including healthcare, transportation, and manufacturing.
 9. AI systems used in employment and workforce management are classified as "high-risk" under the European Union's AI Act.
10. The company's product roadmap includes building a "Nova HR Codex for Global Compliance" to serve as a competitive differentiator.
